The two men are completing formalities in Nanjing to go abroad and are consulting with Minister Zhang. Fan has already gone to Shanghai first, and Deng will go to Shanghai with his family at 5:00 p.m. on the 16th to wait for a ship to go abroad. (Special dispatch, 16th)

The United States is Willing to Fulfill Treaty Obligations in the Far East, but Will Proceed with Prudence. Undersecretary of State Delivers Speech 36

Chicago – Undersecretary of State Phillips recently delivered a speech at the Council on Foreign Relations here, saying, "At this time of frequent incidents and constant changes in the situation in the Far East, our actions should be carried out with a prudent, sympathetic, and patient attitude. The principles we adhere to should be based on safeguarding our national interests, fulfilling our own obligations, and ensuring the universal implementation of all international obligations. All the principles on which existing treaties are based are good for seeking peaceful resolutions to international events. If these principles can be implemented, they will greatly contribute to maintaining peace and justice in the Far East. This is what we firmly believe." He then said that the United States does not want to force any country in the Far East to accept its policies. "We do not want to launch an act of aggression against any country." From the United States' point of view, "the Open Door Policy in China is a good principle. We must not abandon it in any region of China for any country. This is in line with reason and does not violate prudence." Phillips also said that reducing tariff barriers and establishing equal rights in trade are important factors in maintaining peace. Phillips also mentioned that when the Third International met in Moscow last summer, it fully exposed the activities of the Communist Party in the United States. Secretary of State Hull protested to the Soviet government for this. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Chicago – Undersecretary of State Phillips gave a second speech here today, stating that nationalism is at its peak in Asia, but the United States will still uphold the Open Door Policy in China and reiterated what he said in his first speech, that generally speaking, the United States will try to stay out of foreign affairs that are unrelated to it. Secretary of State Hull made a statement last summer stating that if the Soviet government allows activities that interfere in the internal affairs of the United States within its borders, then the United States will find it difficult to continue formal relations with it. Phillips said that the position of the United States has not changed to this day. Phillips said, "Some countries in the Far East are struggling with various difficult problems. The United States does not want to hinder their legitimate solutions. The United States does not want to manipulate others, nor does it want to cause local disputes, and it does not want to take actions that offend any country. We only hope to proceed with a spirit of encouragement and sympathy for various evolutionary and revolutionary developments in the Far East, while vigorously protecting the principles of our own responsibilities and upholding all international responsibilities. If all countries can fulfill existing treaties regarding the Far East, then peace and justice will be close at hand." (National dispatch, 15th)

US Army Budget Submitted to Senate for Discussion 37

The US Army is Insignificant Compared to the Japanese Army

The Army Department recently submitted a budget proposal requiring a total of $559,000,000 in funding. It has been passed by the House of Representatives and submitted to the Senate for discussion. Army Secretary Dern recently gave a speech to reporters, saying that since the late President Wilson until now, the current government has devoted itself to national defense affairs the most. He also said, "If the US Army is compared with the Japanese Army, it is already insignificant. The armaments it is equipped with are only enough to compete with countries with small territories, such as Greece. There is a need to enrich it." Someone asked whether the national defense budget was so large because we were affected by the European situation. Dern replied, "It is true that the United States is not in any danger at the moment, but the unrest in Europe is a fact, and it is very easy for the United States to be drawn into the vortex of European wars. It can be seen from past experience." (Havas dispatch, 15th)

US Conference Held in Argentina 38

Roosevelt's Proposal

President Roosevelt today sent a letter to the President of Argentina and other Latin American presidents, advancing the date of the Pan-American Peace Conference to be held in the Argentine capital or other American capitals, in order to determine the best way to maintain peace in the American republics. He said that this goal can be achieved by immediately ratifying the American peace treaties that have already been negotiated, or by amending existing peace treaties, or by establishing new peace treaties through common coordination. President Roosevelt's intention is that this method can promote world peace, because any treaty that can be established is sufficient to consolidate the efforts of the League of Nations and other existing or future peace organizations. President Roosevelt also stated that the United States is very pleased with the recent agreement between Bolivia and Paraguay and that the Gran Chaco dispute can be resolved forever and justly. The concluding remarks in President Roosevelt's letter read: "The time has come for the American republics to serve the cause of pacifism on this Western continent with outstanding and practical actions." (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Secretary of State Hull gave a speech here today, stating that world peace depends on the development of the economy. Hull did not mention the government's recently announced plan to convene a meeting of American democracies to draft effective peace and neutrality policies. However, observers today are carefully studying his speech to see if there are any hints about South America. Hull said that the destruction of trade opportunities by various countries in the world is one of the greatest threats to world peace today. "If the economic conditions of various countries in the world can be properly managed domestically and can exchange trade in a mutually beneficial way to achieve prosperity, then all feelings of panic and fear will disappear in an instant. At that time, the people of the world will naturally not blindly follow leaders who advocate seeking a way out through war. If the economy cannot prosper, then it is considered that mankind has destroyed its hope and wants to seek glory in the sound of guns. Is this possible?" (National dispatch, 15th)

Capital of Uruguay – The Uruguayan government previously severed diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union because the Communist Party had a general office in the country, hoping to instigate riots in various countries in South America, and seized documents, learning that the party planned to instigate a revolution in the country in the spring. The country's authorities have recently discovered many important documents, and investigations have revealed that Brazilian retired General Prestes is actually the mastermind behind the scenes. He was hiding in the Soviet embassy here. All rebellious movements in various countries in South America, whether in Brazil, Chile, or Uruguay, are presided over by Prestes. This person had sent handwritten letters to various people in Uruguay, with the seal of the Central Committee of the American Communist Party on them, which has been seized by the police. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

The Tragedy of France (Part 2) 40

— Louis Fisher, Translated by Bin Fu

Observation of the European Situation Under the Shadow of War - Part 2

The same indecision troubled France regarding the East African war. Because France had very little direct involvement in the events that occurred in Abyssinia, the French government only wanted to maintain a two-sided approach in the Anglo-Italian crisis. Both of them could be used to contain Germany. When Germany was weak, Franco-Italian friendship was not necessary, and the conflict between Italy and Yugoslavia (France's satellite) certainly made this difficult. In addition, Italy quite wanted to achieve something in the Balkans. But when a resurgent Germany threatened Austria and France, these problems were considered unimportant. The territorial integrity of Austria is also a permanent interest of both France and Italy, thus becoming a bridge for the union of Paris and Rome.

Therefore, in January 1935, Laval ran to Rome to see Mussolini. This decisive meeting was truly a turning point in recent European diplomatic history. Only the Blackshirt leader and Laval knew the whole truth, and they were unwilling to announce it. But some facts are knowable. They agreed that France would withdraw 200,000 troops from the Franco-Italian border and move them to northern France to defend against possible German intrusion. This Franco-Italian agreement also included an understanding between Italy and Yugoslavia, the guarantee of security being that the troops withdrawn by Italy from the Italo-French border would not be moved to the northeast, but would be deployed to a very, very distant place, perhaps East Africa. During the talks in Rome, Laval presented Mussolini with 2,500 shares of the French Djibouti-Addis Ababa Railway and two narrow strips of land (one connecting to southern Libya and the other connecting to Eritrea). At the same time, he also declared in writing the abandonment of the rights granted to France in Abyssinia by the Anglo-Franco-Italian Agreement of December 13, 1906. At the same time, the protracted and unresolved fierce dispute between Britain and Italy over Tunisia was also resolved!! This further reassured Mussolini in Africa and the Mediterranean. In many ways, whether France wanted it or not, the invasion of Abyssinia was simply a product of France.

From the perspective of Franco-Italian relations, this handling by Mussolini and Laval was necessary and smart. From the beginning of the outbreak of the Italo-Ethiopian incident, Laval tried his best to continue the policy of Franco-Italian friendship. However, Italy was only occupying worthless land in Africa. They had already divided up the fertile land. Britain had cooperated with Italy on naval issues in order to temporarily oppose France. Now that Italy was on France's side, Britain would naturally not think of any cooperation again.

When Great Britain hesitated about Italy and Abyssinia, things stagnated. In May 1935, London became greatly distraught. By June, she decided to act. In preparation for the duel, she signed the Anglo-German Naval Agreement on June 18, 1935. The result caused a shock in Paris. Had the faithless "Albion" (the ancient name of England) returned? On February 3, Britain and France had jointly worked together in London for European peace, especially involving Germany. In the second week of April, the two powers had also agreed on the German issue. Unexpectedly, since then, as Paris said, Great Britain betrayed France and suddenly concluded a naval agreement with Germany that was detrimental to France, putting France in a disadvantageous position against Germany.

All these grudges could not induce France to cooperate with Britain on the Italo-Ethiopian issue. But Britain needed this cooperation and therefore insisted on it. If the British fleet were once pressed by Italian ships, it would need to take refuge in French Mediterranean ports. But would France allow them to enter? If France opposed them, the League of Nations would not seem to decide on sanctions. France hesitated. So Laval asked in return, if we are attacked by Germany, do you intend to act? Mr. Samuel Hoare frankly replied that he did not know; that it would depend on the circumstances; that it should have "Elasticity". France did not like these. Britain exerted great pressure on Paris, and Laval was forced to agree to economic sanctions. In the third week of October, just before the final resolution of the League of Nations, when the French government tried its best to oppose the embargo on Italian goods, Anglo-French relations almost broke down. Documents flew back and forth like snowflakes. France was ultimately afraid of breaking with London, and finally succumbed to Britain's orders.

Britain blamed France's tactics for delaying the implementation of economic sanctions, encouraging Mussolini to believe in the League of Nations' concessions and its behind-the-scenes mediation. Although French government personnel guaranteed that France would abide by its sanctions obligations, Parisian newspapers and many businessmen always hated sanctions, and perhaps secret trafficking of goods was still not prevented. France outwardly insisted on permanent negotiations to resolve the Abyssinian War. It is said that Britain's participation in these expert meetings was to prevent France from concluding articles with Rome that were unfavorable to London.

Britain resented France's attitude. But their resentment was much milder than that of France. France deeply felt that she had lost her independence in diplomacy. If it were necessary to explore one between Britain and Italy, France would naturally take Britain. Britain would be of more help in resisting Germany. But France harbored a fantasy of simultaneously reconciling with London and Rome, just like they shook hands with Moscow while at the same time courting Berlin. The tragedy of France lies in the refusal to choose one of the two, resulting in the loss of both. The Bolsheviks were deeply displeased by France's wooing of the "Nazis," but Franco-German rapprochement remained very slim. France's cooperation with Britain on sanctions hurt Italy, but at the same time, France's indecision still failed to generate special goodwill from Britain.

Page 8

The Abyssinian army appears to be trying to prevent the Italian forces from advancing to the city of Bali, and is making every effort to organize the supply and sanitation of its troops in order to sustain a long-term effort. The main road from Adua to Magala has been completely severed by the Abyssinian army, and roads from Magala to other places have also been rendered impassable by the Abyssinian army. It is reported that the Italian forces are now using airplanes to drop military supplies by parachute to resupply the garrison at Magala. One day, a strong wind blew several of the Italian planes' parachutes over the Abyssinian lines. The Abyssinian army did not initially know that the Italian forces were using this method to resupply the garrison at Magala. After obtaining the food attached to the parachutes, they were very suspicious and did not dare to eat it. They first fed it to dogs, and then dared to eat it themselves. The son of the Abyssinian envoy to London, Martin, was traveling in a heavy truck from Huardia to Taixi today when he was heavily bombarded by Italian artillery. He narrowly escaped injury, but shrapnel flew over his head and struck a person sitting next to him, causing one of their eyes to pop out. A member of the Tikori tribe, under General Siyum, died this afternoon when an Italian plane dropped dozens of bombs, and a bottle of wine fell on his head, causing his skull to shatter. The plane was flying at an altitude of several thousand feet, and none of the bombs dropped hit their targets. (Reuters, 16th)

This planned action occurred only a few days after the bombing of Olho Hodoga. The authorities have decided to respond with a policy of ensuring border security.

Tokyo (Domei, 16th) - Regarding the Jinchan Valley incident, Ambassador Ota met with Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Stoermoniakov on the 14th. Foreign Ministry officials have stated their position on this matter: the participation of a third country in the Japanese-Manchukuoan-Soviet on-site mixed investigation committee is not only meaningless, but would also hinder the on-site investigation, which can be conducted more satisfactorily among the three countries directly involved. The army has not yet contacted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, but the general opinion of the army leadership is as follows: The proposal to establish a mixed Japanese-Manchukuoan-Soviet committee was made because of frequent disputes on the Manchu-Soviet border, all caused by the unclear border. Therefore, it is considered necessary to establish a clear border. The decision should be made by commissioners appointed by the countries directly involved. Therefore, there is no need to appoint a representative from a third country to participate as a commissioner. However, in order to resolve disputes amicably, it would be permissible to agree to a third country sending a commissioner as an observer to conduct an impartial investigation.

He believes that Outer Mongolian troops, instigated by Soviet Russia, have extended their outposts to within the territory that Japan considers to be "Manchukuo." The most impartial opinion here is that Soviet Russia is currently focused on increasing its domestic industrial strength and is unlikely to take offensive action. At the same time, Japan is unlikely to launch a rash attack before obtaining German guarantees of military cooperation. (Japanese Ambassador to Russia Ota held talks with Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Stoermoniakov yesterday regarding the Russian-"Manchukuoan" border conflict. The Times has written an article commenting on the matter and discussing the Far Eastern situation, stating, "Japan's policy in Manchuria has remained unchanged since the establishment of 'Manchukuo.' Its aim is to establish a strong 'anti-communist' front throughout North China. There is no doubt about this. As far as the Soviet Union is concerned, a direct war with Japan would be a dangerous experiment for the Soviet system, so it is advantageous to avoid war. As for Japan, there are many internal financial and economic difficulties, and it is busy consolidating the new position it has created in Manchuria and North China. How can it ignore everything and engage in a large-scale war on the Asian continent? From this point of view, although Japanese-Russian relations are currently strained, they are unlikely to lead to a formal war." (Havas, 15th)

Paris (Havas, 15th) - French political circles are taking a calm approach to the Japanese-Russian border conflict, considering it not very serious. The French government is currently most concerned with German rearmament, Austrian independence, the assault on Socialist leader Léon Blum, and the upcoming general election. However, France has significant interests in the Far East and is particularly concerned about developments there due to its recent mutual assistance agreement with Soviet Russia. Although the French-Russian mutual assistance agreement is limited to Europe and does not apply to an unprovoked Japanese attack on Soviet Russia, French political circles believe that the agreement should exert a moderating influence on peace between Japan and Russia. They also believe that Japan is unlikely to attack Soviet Russia now, because since the agreement has been concluded, Soviet Russia's rear is protected by France and is not threatened by German attacks. However, the agreement is also sufficient to prevent Soviet Russia from attacking Japan, because Soviet Russia cannot obtain French assistance to jointly resist Japan. Spanish Lower House Re-election 46

Madrid (Havas, 15th) - The Lower House, dissolved on January 7th of this year, is now scheduled for re-election tomorrow. According to the constitution, each province is a constituency, except for provinces with important cities, which divide the provincial capital and the rest of the province into two constituencies, such as Barcelona and Madrid. Each constituency elects one member of the Lower House for every 50,000 residents. A total of 473 members of the Lower House are elected nationwide. In order to prevent one party or a group of parties from monopolizing each constituency, the list of candidates submitted by each party must not exceed 80% of the total number of seats in that constituency. In order for the election of "majority list" candidates to be valid, one of the candidates must receive at least 40% of the total number of votes cast. The remaining seats, i.e., 20%, will be allocated to the "absolute majority" list, provided that one of the candidates receives 20% of the total number of votes cast. If no one receives 40% of the total number of votes cast in the first round of voting, a second round of voting will be held on March 1st. Only those who received at least 8% of the votes in the first round of voting will be allowed to participate in the second round.

Madrid (Havas, 15th) - The election of the Lower House is scheduled to take place tomorrow. Robles, the leader of the right-wing Popular Action Party, recently delivered a speech to party members, summing up the election campaign. The speech was broadcast by radio to over 400 cities and towns, stating, "Our party is confident of victory in tomorrow's election. However, party members must continue to work hard and not slacken in the slightest, ensuring that not a single vote is lost."

Random Artistic Thoughts

Tangram 52

— Feng Zikai

A young man enthusiastic about learning to paint came to ask me: "How can one learn to paint successfully?" Faced with this broad question, I really couldn't think of an answer for a moment. But he sat upright, his eyes fixed on my lips, as if expecting some secrets of painting to fall from them. In an instant, I turned my thoughts to the most common fault of painting learners, copying others' work, and hurriedly replied: "How can one learn to paint successfully? It's hard to say in a word. The fundamental method can be said to be to give equal importance to hand and eye. That is, one must not only practice the depiction of the wrist, but also practice the observation of the eyes." What I meant was that learning to paint must start with sketching from life, and one should not merely imitate the works of others. Because the life of a painting exists in the objects, and certainly not in painting books.

After studying for a while, the young man came back to ask me: "How can one learn to paint successfully?" Looking at his past achievements, I saw that they mostly focused on details while ignoring the overall picture, so the objects he painted lost their reality. So I told him again: "When sketching from life, one should not focus on details but on the overall picture, and strive to make the whole thing look like the real thing." What I meant was that his observation was not precise enough, seeing the small and forgetting the big, so his depiction was not entirely correct.

After studying for a while, the young man came back to ask me: "How can one learn to paint successfully?" Looking at his past achievements, although they were better than before, the shapes were still not correct. So I told him again: "The first thing to pay attention to when sketching from life is 'shape.' Whether it's details or the overall picture, if the shape is not correct, the foundation of the painting is not stable." What I meant was that his depiction of shapes was not entirely correct and he needed to pay more attention to observation.

After studying for a while, the young man came back to ask me: "How can one learn to paint successfully?" Looking at his past achievements, they were much better than before, but the shapes were still not completely correct, and he still couldn't fully take care of both details and the overall picture, meaning that his observing eyes were not fully trained. So, using more abstract words, I told him again: "The first thing to learn when painting is to write out the 'spirit' of the object, and not just paint the rigid form." What I meant was that I hoped he would broaden his horizons, capture the characteristics of the object, and depict the spirit of the object.

However, these words were too abstract, confusing the young art student and simply stopping his painting studies. I was very sorry, wishing I could share some of my physical feelings with him to complete the work that was only one basket short. One day, I met this young man again somewhere, and a child next to him was playing with a tangram. I saw him putting together the shape of a person, using only two kinds of shapes: squares, triangles, and parallelograms (malt candy-shaped). Although simple and not concerned with details, the overall picture looked very much like a person, and the spirit was vivid. Seeing this, I seemed to have an epiphany, and said to the young man on the spur of the moment: "Learning to paint should take the tangram as a model!" The young man suddenly understood under this sentence, and his subsequent achievements suddenly improved, all with artistic intent.

This saying is very similar to Zen Buddhism, which seems unbelievable; however, it is based on the principles of painting. Originally, the most important thing in painting is the depiction of the overall posture. The spirit of the object lies in this, and the life of the painting lies in this. With the overall picture, even if the details are ignored, it doesn't matter much. On the contrary, if the overall picture is not correct, even if the details are very precise, it is in vain. We can take daily life as an example; doctors are like looking at people. When your friend walks from a distance, even if you haven't seen the eyebrows clearly, you can tell who it is just by the overall posture. On the contrary, if you only look at one hand, or only look at a small part of the eyebrows, even if it is an acquaintance, it is not easy to recognize for a while. Also, like looking at scenery, viewing the shape of mountains from a distance, like screens, like banners, like cows, like lions, like summer clouds, like melancholy eyebrows. What you see is the spirit of the mountain. On the contrary, if you enter the mountain and look at the details, you will not see its spirit, or even not feel that you are in the mountain. Looking at willows from a distance, like smoke, like mist, like drunkards, like sleepers. What you see is the spirit of the willow. On the contrary, if you walk close to the willow and look at the details, you will not see its spirit, and it seems like another kind of tree. Watching movies should sit far away, and looking at paintings should step back a few steps, all because distant viewing can see the overall picture and see the spirit. It can be seen that the spirit of the object is not in the details but in the overall picture. If you want to capture the spirit in painting, you must pay attention to the depiction of the overall posture.

Among the expressions of images, nothing focuses on the overall picture more than the tangram, or the puzzle board made of thirteen pieces. The simplicity of their tools forces them to focus on the overall picture. However, if they are put together cleverly, not only are the shape and spirit very similar, but they also leave room for people to imagine, which is quite artistic. Although this is a kind of toy, it implies the key points of painting. General elementary school students use painting books, and beginners use painting manuals, which mostly start from geometric shapes such as squares and triangles; when sketching from life, the first draft must be made with straight lines, even if you draw a ball, you must first use straight lines to enclose it, all based on this painting principle. In detail, before holding a pen, learners should first make an overall observation of the object, ignoring its detailed points, but regarding it as a phenomenon composed of various geometric shapes such as triangles, squares, and rectangles. The first draft of the painting may as well be expressed with geometric shapes first, and then, based on this overall picture, add detailed descriptions one by one. In this way, no matter how detailed the description is, the overall picture will always be correct, meaning that the spirit of the object will always be preserved. The reason why the young art student succeeded was that he embarked on this great path of learning to paint.

Learning to paint must start with the overall picture. This does not mean that detailed description is useless, but that the overall picture is more important, and the details are less important. In detail, there are only three kinds of paintings: those that take care of both the overall picture and the details, those that take care of the overall picture and ignore the details, and those that take care of the details and ignore the overall picture. The first two are good, and the first one is a good meticulous painting. Religious paintings of the Renaissance, works of the classical school, the romantic school, and the realist school all belong to this category. The second type is a good rough painting or simple painting. Works of expressionism, fauvism, and various sketches and comics all belong to this category. Only the last third type, which takes care of the details and ignores the overall picture, is a poor product. Like some kinds of monthly calendars that are popular in our country now, flower papers sold everywhere in the lunar New Year, and most of the picture cards wrapped in cigarettes, all belong to this category. In these paintings, the depictions are probably very detailed, and the colors are red, green, and gold. They are eye-catching at first glance, and the details are very delicate when viewed closely, but when viewed from a distance, the overall picture is not right! The proportions are inappropriate, the parts are unnatural, the shapes are incorrect, so they are not like real things, and there is no spirit; even to the point of being strange and making people laugh or fear.

People who lack artistic education, people with low-level tastes, do not know the overall picture of painting, and the exquisiteness and brightness of the parts can satisfy their aesthetic desires. They are the admirers of the above-mentioned third type of painting. In the world, especially in our country, this kind of admirer accounts for the majority. So art is often difficult to develop properly. Therefore, artists of the past often hid in ivory towers because their music was too high and few could harmonize.

Therefore, I am now using the analogy of the tangram to explain the key points of painting, not only for beginners of painting. I hope that the general public also has this bit of artistic appreciation. February 3, 25th year [of the Republic of China, i.e. 1936]
