Guangdong Province Expands Civil Aviation 68

Beihai Civil Aerodrome Expands Area Recent Expansion of Zhong-Fa Yue-He Route Operated by China National Aviation Corporation

Guangzhou correspondence: Guangdong Province has recently been expanding civil aviation. Southwest Aviation Corporation has been raising funds to open the Guangdong-Jiangxi civil aviation route. The provincial government has also been building climate measurement stations in various places in Nanlu to facilitate the flight of civil aircraft. Hepu County in Nanlu is the first county in Lianzhou and borders Guangxi Province. The area is a major route for civil aviation between Guangdong and Guangxi. The county magistrate previously suggested expanding the Beihai Aerodrome in the county. Yesterday, the provincial government decided to instruct the Suggestion Department to order Southwest Aviation Corporation to draft and reply to the aerodrome expansion plan. The methods have been drafted and submitted to the Construction Department. The department ordered the Hepu County Government to follow the instructions. The Beihai Civil Aerodrome in Hepu County originally planned to expand the area to 30,100.0 acres, 1,400 feet wide from north to south, and 2,150 feet long from east to west. Compared with the original area, the expansion is more than doubled, which is very suitable for aircraft take-off and landing, but it requires more than 80,000 yuan. Later, due to difficulties in raising funds, the Civil Aviation Corporation revised the method, temporarily not acquiring houses or relocating graves, and only expanding the north and south boundaries of the original aerodrome to 870 feet and the east and west boundaries to 1,600 feet. In this way, it can save the cost of buying land and houses, so it is now expanding according to this plan. Yesterday, the Hepu County Government was ordered to comply.

Southwest Aviation Corporation originally planned to operate the China-Vietnam route (i.e., from Guangdong and Guangxi to French Vietnam). Later, the Ministry of Transportation designated the China-France route to be operated by China National Aviation Corporation. The Guangxi authorities repeatedly telegraphed Nanjing to fight for it, but it was ultimately ineffective. Recently, China National Aviation Corporation has been preparing to send aircraft to fly the route, and will use new type Kesai aircraft to fly. The route is extended from the Shanghai-Guangdong route to Hanoi, French Annam, and is officially named the Guangdong-Hanoi route. It is scheduled to start operations at the end of this month. In order to connect with the Shanghai-Guangdong route, it is planned to change the schedule to fly from Shanghai to Guangdong on Mondays and Thursdays, and return north on Wednesdays and Saturdays, with two flights each way. The schedule for the Guangdong-Hanoi route is scheduled to be once a week on Fridays, arriving on the same day. The flight time and ticket price are as follows: Westbound flight, aircraft departing from Guangzhou at 6:30 a.m. on Friday, arriving at Sai Gon, French Annam at 8:30 a.m., aircraft departing from Sai Gon at 8:50 a.m., arriving at Hanoi, French Annam at 11:15 a.m. Eastbound flight, aircraft departing from Hanoi at 12:00 noon, arriving at Sai Gon at 2:25 p.m., aircraft departing from Sai Gon at 2:45 p.m., arriving at Guangzhou at 4:40 p.m. The stopover at the Sai Gon station is only 20 minutes. Ticket price, one way, each passenger from Guangzhou to Sai Gon, national currency 100 yuan, from Guangzhou to Hanoi 200 yuan, from Sai Gon to Hanoi 100 yuan. Round trip, from Guangzhou to Sai Gon, national currency 180 yuan, to Hanoi 260 yuan, from Sai Gon to Hanoi 180 yuan. Passengers traveling to Hanoi can transfer to the France-operated Europe-Asia route to fly directly to Paris. (February 12)

A Record of Life in the Desert (4) 69

— Jin Dui

5. A Glimpse of the People's Livelihood in Hexi, Gansu

The Yellow River originates from the Gadasuqi Lao Mountain in Qinghai, meandering and converging across the territory of Gansu Province. What is now called Hexi is, from the perspective of Gansu, a corner of China. Hexi is located in the center of Gansu, Qinghai, Ningxia, Xinjiang, and Inner Mongolia, with an area of 398,514 square miles and a population of 1,112,284. Its terrain is strategically important, and its residents are numerous. On the one hand, it can control the border of Xinjiang and Mongolia, and on the other hand, it can shield the vicinity of Ningxia and Qinghai. It is very important in terms of national defense and economy. However, due to the obstruction of mountains and rivers and the inconvenience of transportation, the atmosphere is stagnant and the culture is backward, which is despised by the people of the inland. Because of a fleeting glimpse, I can only briefly describe the major aspects of the people's livelihood as follows:

"Customs" The customs and habits of a place are precisely the symbol of the people's lives in that place. This is true, isn't it? The folk customs of Hexi are not as extravagant as those in the big cities of the inland. Their customs are ancient and their folk customs are simple and honest. Most of the rural families live by farming or animal husbandry. They work tirelessly throughout the year, saving every penny they earn and not wasting it. There is no extravagance at all. Men are either engaged in farming, animal husbandry, or business, and women weave behind closed doors, all able to support themselves with a skill. However, in this simple and ancient custom, there are three very bad habits, which are indeed flaws in the white jade and a worrying problem in the Northwest: The prevalence of keeping long hair and foot binding; the ignorance and stubbornness of superstitious idols; the prevalence of opium smoking.

In Hexi, funerals follow ancient customs. Children wear mourning clothes for their parents for three years, and nephews and grandchildren wear them for two years; cousins wear them for three to nine months, depending on the degree of kinship. Usually, men marry at the age of eighteen and women at the age of fifteen or sixteen. However, early marriage is common everywhere. It is said that there are also "betrothals in the womb" and keeping "child brides." Marriage also follows ancient rituals, but recently, in cities and large towns, it has gradually become possible to see civilized weddings that combine Chinese and Western styles or are fully Westernized. "Products" Hexi has a vast area and abundant resources, so its products are very rich. The crops in the entire area include beans, wheat, sorghum, millet, highland barley, tobacco, as well as large-scale plants and animals such as cattle, horses, sheep, and camels. In terms of medicinal materials, rhubarb is abundant in the Qilian Mountains; wolfberries in Minqin, cistanche deserticola in Linze; licorice in Yumen and Ganta; astragalus membranaceus in Gaotai; and cynomorium songaricum, musk, and deer antler in Ganliang are all very famous.

As for mineral products, there are even more reserves, distributed all over the place. Gold, silver, copper, iron, lead, coal, petroleum, sulfur, and salt are both complete and abundant. It is a pity that most of them have not been mined, so the treasures are hidden in the ground, only arousing the ambition of outsiders to covet them. If new methods can be used to invest in large-scale development, then the financial resources will be opened up, the economy will be abundant, and the people of the desert will live a comfortable life.

"Education" Culture is the driving force of social progress. If culture cannot be promoted, social life cannot move forward. The social life of Hexi has been delayed in its progress in this undeveloped culture. This is partly due to natural disasters - the prevalence of floods, droughts, and plagues, and man-made disasters - the spread of banditry and arson. The people are in a state of displacement and hardship, unable to provide for themselves with food and clothing, let alone raise funds, so education is difficult to develop. According to the investigation, there are a total of four secondary schools: one each for the Wuwei Provincial Second Normal School and the Provincial Fourth Middle School; one for the Jiuquan Provincial Fourth Normal School; and one for the Zhangye Junior High School. The total annual expenditure of the four schools is more than 30,000 yuan. The monthly salary of teachers and staff is no more than 100 yuan at the highest and only 6 yuan at the lowest. The treatment of primary school teachers is even more meager. The annual salary of an average teacher is at most less than 120 yuan, and the lowest is only 20 to 30 yuan. Can such a difficult and tight budget allow for successful and complete school education? Therefore, many adopt a perfunctory policy. The textbooks for primary schools actually still use ancient books such as the "Three Character Classic" as teaching materials. This may be due to the undeveloped local atmosphere and the conservative nature of old scholars. However, the educational situation in Hexi can already be seen.

6. The Current Situation of Animal Husbandry in Gansu

Gansu has interlaced rivers and abundant grasslands, and its natural conditions are most suitable for animal husbandry. What's more, it should also meet the needs of the environment. According to the latest survey, the following is listed for reference by those who are interested in improving animal husbandry in the Northwest.

(A) Types and Pastoral Areas The most numerous type of livestock is sheep, followed by cattle, horses, donkeys, mules, camels, etc. The areas with more developed animal husbandry in Gansu Province are Haiyuan County in the east, followed by Guyuan and Huining. In the south of the province, Linze, Minxian, Xiahe, and Xigu counties produce a particularly large number of livestock. The yak, hairy cattle, and Fanheiyang sheep produced there are very famous. In Yongdeng, Minqin, Shandan, Yongchang and other counties in the west of the province, animal husbandry is also flourishing. In Liancheng Songshan, which belongs to Yongdeng County, it is common to see Fan people raising thousands of cattle and horses, plus one or two thousand sheep. In addition to herding sheep, the people of Minqin County also raise thousands of camels. In the past, the so-called "Zhenfan Ma family" raised more than 20,000 camels in one household. The prosperity of animal husbandry can be seen. Jingyuan and Jingtai counties in the west of the province are said to produce abundant sheep, and the lambskin produced in Dalu and Xiaolutang is said to be no less than that of Ningxia.

(B) Pastures Animal husbandry in Gansu is mostly carried out by individual households, breeding and living on the land. There are very few organizations such as animal husbandry companies or joint animal husbandry farms. In the past, there were horse farms in Ganzhou (Zhangye), Liangzhou (Wuwei), Suzhou (Jiuquan), and Xining (now belonging to Qinghai), which were managed by the government. The number of horses raised in the horse farms reached more than 30,000. However, they have all been destroyed by years of war. During the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, a farm was set up in Dama Camp, which was under the jurisdiction of Gulang County, to graze and raise more than 1,000 horses. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, it was changed to a stud farm, and then three branch farms were set up in Haiyuan Pingfan (under the jurisdiction of Yongdeng County) and Maxianshan (under the jurisdiction of Gaolan County), all of which were under the jurisdiction of the Military Department of the Provincial Government. Before long, they were successively closed and disappeared. The more famous private pastures are Liancheng Songshan Beach (under the jurisdiction of Yongdeng County), Beihai (under the jurisdiction of Minqin County), and Huangyan Lake (under the jurisdiction of Wuwei County), which have a wide range. As for Dalu and Xiaolutang, Wufosi, and various places in Xiahe County, there is livestock everywhere and grazing everywhere.

(C) Feeding The feeding methods of livestock mostly rely on nature in the folk. In places where water and grass are abundant, they are grazed at will. Large groups are mostly chosen to be placed in suitable locations on the grasslands, foothills, or river beaches, and then simple stables are built to provide a place to rest at night. Large livestock such as mules and horses must be fed bran and hay once every night when they return to the stable. Cattle and sheep are only fed hay on snowy days in winter. The hay is mostly cut from the mountains in early autumn and transported to houses to be stored for feeding on snowy nights. The amount of artificial feeding is also described below. Mule and horse feed - half beans and oats, and 2 catties of bran each, and 3 catties of grass. Excellent horses are fed bran every day, and ordinary horses are either fed feed or bran, not both. Cattle are fed 3 catties of hay in winter snow, and are not fed bran and are forbidden to use it, for fear of damaging the spleen. After giving birth, they are kept in the circle for seven days and fed broad bean noodle soup to make it easier to produce milk. Sheep are fed one and a half catties of grass on snowy nights. After giving birth, they are kept in the circle for three days and fed grass and noodle soup to make milk. Camels need to eat 3 catties of small beans and half a catty of green salt every day. The above quantities are based on the investigation in Gaolan County. Other counties may have minor differences but are generally the same.

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

Lecture on History Foreign History (2) 70

— Professor Shen Gangbo of Central University

What I just said is the common point of all history. But foreign history is really more useful for modern Chinese youth. Because it can make up for the shortcomings of national history. The virtues of our nation are filial piety, brotherhood, benevolence, righteousness, diligence, thrift, and peace; what is lacking is the spirit of being public and forgetting self, forgetting family for the country, not avoiding difficulties and dangers, and fighting to the end. In the national history, there are certainly many models of doing one's best and sacrificing oneself to save others, but at the same time, it is also full of the theories and deeds of the Huang-Lao school. As a result, the spirit of self-improvement, becoming benevolent, and taking righteousness is often neutralized and offset by the theory of protecting oneself wisely and being pure and inactive, making it equal to zero. As for foreign history, there are only examples of the former and very few discussions of the latter. Isn't it the most sufficient to save the evils of Chinese traditional thought? There is another layer. Chinese history books are mostly official histories. Those who are ordered to write history are certainly knowledgeable, but they are always inevitably constrained by political power and cannot escape the scope of orthodox thought. Therefore, they are not very free in selecting materials and recording facts. The conclusions they reach are naturally difficult to fully agree with the truth. Therefore, Mencius said long ago: "It is better to have no books than to believe them all." This is the difficulty of learning Chinese history. Young students have little experience in the world and limited opinions. If no one guides them, it is difficult to obtain the truth from it. As for foreign history, they are all private works. They have great freedom and are not much constrained by external forces. In addition, their sociology and archeology are very advanced. The history written using scientific methods and with the help of science is naturally more precise and in line with the truth. Therefore, if young students want to cultivate the freedom of thought, practice the precision of observation, and train the correctness of judgment, it is most beneficial to read more foreign history books.

From this point of view, foreign history can not only give us a scientific spirit, but also mold our great personality. Its use is so great, can we still say that it has nothing to do with me and that learning it is a waste of time?

The second objection to teaching foreign history in middle schools is due to a misunderstanding of the content of foreign history in middle schools. Middle school students learning foreign history do not need to be completely, "exhaustively learned and widely heard." All the excitement of wars, the trivial matters of the court, the sacred traces of religions, the art of gold and stone, the anecdotes of celebrities, the allusions of the literary world, and the research of those bronze swords, stone axes, broken bowls, and broken bricks are all matters for history experts, and middle school students do not need to worry about them. What middle school students should know is only the general outline of the changes in foreign political and legal systems, the overview of the evolution of economic organizations, and the direction of the development of academic thought. Knowing these, they can have a correct understanding of the trend of the world and can also understand the modern international situation and the relations between various countries and us. Therefore, the content of foreign history in middle schools is not in breadth but in essence, not in quantity but in quality. So, what standard should be used to select materials? The Italian historian Croce said: "The characteristic of history is the modernization of its thought. All records that are irrelevant to the present are not considered history." This statement is quite problematic in the eyes of history experts. But if it is used as a standard for middle school students to choose historical materials, it is very correct. Therefore, I advise everyone to read foreign history according to Croce's proposal. When encountering something, first ask whether it is directly or indirectly related to today's world. If there is a relationship, then even if the matter is small, it should be noted. If it is irrelevant, then even if it is interesting in itself, you don't have to care about it. For example, the first people to arrive in the Americas may have been the Vikings of Northern Europe or even earlier Chinese people. Experts can devote their entire lives to studying this problem. As for middle school students, they can ignore it. Because in any case, the development of the Americas began after Columbus went there. The Vikings who had been to California before and the Chinese who had been to Canada really had no influence on the New World and no contribution to the Old World. Studying them is not enough to help us understand today's America, so why should we care about it? To give another example, in Greek history, they all talk about the Peloponnesian War, and in Roman history, they all talk about the Punic War. These two events were indeed extremely important to ancient Greece and Rome; if they are regarded as moral lessons, they are also quite valuable. But let me ask, how has the collapse of the Athenian Empire hindered the development of modern civilian politics; how has the temporary dominance of Sparta had anything to do with the prevalence of militarism today; and how has Hannibal's world-famous reputation affected Europe and Africa today? So, why should middle school students bother to remember them? There are quite a few similar records in a small foreign history textbook. The wars and temporary systems of many dynasties are not necessarily related to the present. If we can all use the three words "modernity" as the standard for studying Western history, we can simplify the complex and save trouble.

The third group of people advocates exploring the glorious history of our country to promote national spirit, which is correct. But to say that learning foreign history can easily be confused by heresies and shake one's own good traditional ideas is to know only one thing and not the other. The history of mankind is originally a whole, and the cultures of the world are all related to each other. If you don't ask about the whole history, but only learn the partial history, that is like blind men touching an elephant, and you will never really recognize the elephant! For example, the most powerful era of the Han people was none other than the Han and Tang Dynasties. Let me ask, can you fully understand the political facilities of the Han and Tang Dynasties without understanding the foreign situation at that time? What is most related to today is the Qing Dynasty. Let me ask, can you successfully study the history of the past hundred years without knowing foreign history? As for the history of the Song and Yuan Dynasties, it is intricately related to foreign history everywhere, which is even more unnecessary to say. Not only politics, but also academics. Our country's calendar, mathematics, medicine, art, music, religious beliefs, clothing, decoration, and even the study of rhymes and initials, and the theory of understanding the mind and seeing the nature, have all been influenced by foreign cultures. If we want to trace the roots and understand the national conditions, we really have to refer to foreign history. For example, if a person wants to understand the words and deeds of his grandfather and father, it is not enough to only know his grandfather and father. You also have to know the friends and relatives who often interact with his grandfather and father. Even the servants they used and the enemies they fought with must be known. Therefore, it is said that to promote national quintessence, we must never adopt an attitude of deep closure and isolation.

Moreover, today is not an era of pioneering. If we don't understand the true appearance of foreign countries, we will have no way to deal with foreign countries. The foreign countries of today have all evolved from their past history. If we don't know their history, we will never understand their current situation, and we will have no way to judge their gains and losses, predict their future, and formulate a response policy. To give an example, the world today is actually dominated by three doctrines: liberalism, communism, and fascism. Why can only Britain and France maintain freedom? Why can Russia implement communism? Why is fascism prevalent in Italy and Germany? I would say that you can't find the reason for it without looking at the history of the past two hundred years. If you don't know their special historical background, how can you criticize its good or bad, predict its success or failure, and decide our attitude towards it? The failure of the Reform Movement in the late Qing Dynasty, the failure of the trial of parliamentary politics in the early Republic of China, the damage to China's vitality by the recent communist movement, and the fact that various imported doctrines do not fully conform to the national conditions and only disturb the people are all because they only know the fur of foreign countries and do not understand its historical background. If we can thoroughly understand the causes and consequences of various doctrines, we will naturally know how to determine the national conditions, judge the urgency, and use the most economical and appropriate methods to learn from others' strengths, make up for our own weaknesses, and innovate and build with half the effort. How can we blindly follow others and repeatedly go the wrong way, cutting our feet to fit the shoes, and failing to draw a tiger well? People often say "know yourself and your enemy." If we really want to "know them," we need to learn their history; to thoroughly "know ourselves," we also need to refer to and compare their history. In short, if you don't have the knowledge of world history, it is impossible to be a useful citizen today.

But learning foreign history is not enough to know many fragmented historical materials. Any knowledge must be thorough; a half-baked understanding is very dangerous. A few years ago, a diplomat went to the United States and talked to reporters, saying: "The three northeastern provinces have become the Alsace-Lorraines of the East." He only knew that France and Germany had become sworn enemies due to the dispute over Alsace-Lorraine, which affected the whole of Europe; he did not know that the historical relationship between the Germans and Alsace-Lorraine was completely different from the historical relationship between the Japanese and the three northeastern provinces. Quoting allusions wrongly not only loses the national image unconsciously, but is also tantamount to speaking for the Japanese. From this point of view, if you don't really learn foreign history thoroughly, you will be clever and far-fetched, not only making a fool of yourself, but also causing great trouble.

If you want to learn thoroughly, you have to study the method of learning thoroughly. After all the middle school students go to college in the future, whether they study science and engineering, or medicine and agriculture, they may never have the opportunity to formally study foreign history again. This bit of foreign history knowledge all depends on what you learn in middle school. If you want to learn thousands of years of world history thoroughly in a short period of a few years, you must have a method of controlling complexity with simplicity. Memorizing the book to death is of no use.

If you want to get the method of studying history, you must first determine the attitude of reading history. The same book, "the benevolent see benevolence, and the wise see wisdom." If the views are different, the methods will naturally be different. Therefore, if you want to know a good historical method, you must first develop a normal historical concept. Those who have studied history in the past have talked about "subtle words and great meanings" and "praising and criticizing penmanship," which is to find ethical lessons in history with a philosophical attitude. Some specialize in discussing natural disasters and man-made disasters, good and evil, cause and effect, which is a religious concept to seek theological arguments in history. Some carefully examine words and sentences, appreciate historical writing, and say that Thucydides' records are concise and meaningful, and Gibbon's narratives are vivid. This is to find the beauty of art in history with a literary eye. There are also people who advocate the superhuman view of history, regarding a history as the deeds of a few heroes. Some people boast about the "national historical view," regarding all human culture as the creation of their own race. Some people expound the "materialist historical view," regarding people as ants and bees, as if everything in the past and present is nothing but a struggle for food and clothing - these are all using a politician's attitude to find their propaganda materials in history. These people have their own prejudices, and therefore have their own methods, but none of them are the proper attitude to study history, especially not the historical concept that middle school students should have. Because history is not philosophy, not literature, and even less a political tool; it is really the process of the evolution of the entire human race. Therefore, we should use the concept of evolution and the scientific attitude to seek the laws of human evolution in it. Students who study "natural history" study small animals and plants in the same way; they should use magnifying glasses to see its entirety clearly, and then use microscopes to carefully examine its organization; they must never wear colored glasses and see everything in a different color! (To be continued)

Page 10

General Situation of Sichuan Provincial Government's Implementation of New Policies in the First Year of Establishment 71

——Report by Deng Mingjie at the Anniversary Commemoration——

Chengdu Air Dispatch: The Sichuan Provincial Government was established in Chongqing on February 10th of last year. The 10th of this month marks its first anniversary. At 9:00 AM that day, officials from various departments and offices of the Provincial Government gathered in the Provincial Government's main office building to hold a celebration ceremony. More than 800 people attended, including Secretary-General Deng Mingjie, Director Fei Dongming, Commissioner Xie Peiyun, secretaries and section chiefs of various departments and offices, heads of various sections, and staff at all levels. After performing the ceremonial rites, Secretary-General Deng delivered a detailed and pertinent report on the work of the Provincial Government in the past year and the future direction of its efforts. The full text of his speech is recorded as follows:

"Fellow colleagues, today is the anniversary of the establishment of the Provincial Government. The significance of our celebration here lies in reviewing the past and encouraging the future. Taking this opportunity, I would like to briefly report to you on the progress of the past year. Since its establishment last year, Chairman Liu believes that the Provincial Government bears three major missions: unifying the entire Sichuan, alleviating the suffering of the people, and building a new Sichuan. These will be briefly described separately below.

Unifying Sichuan First, unifying Sichuan. Because in the past, there was the division of defense zones, which invisibly divided the entire Sichuan into several small provinces. Although there was a legitimate provincial government in name, in fact, none of the government orders were thoroughly implemented. At the beginning of the new Provincial Government's establishment, the Chairman and all the commissioners believed that if the defense zones were not broken, the Provincial Government would still become an organization with only a name but no substance in the future. Therefore, while reporting their assumption of office, they telegraphed the leaders of various armies, stating the significance of recovering political power and completing unification. Fortunately, the leaders of various armies were able to take the overall situation into consideration, and in a very short period of time, they all agreed to return political power to the Provincial Government. In order to make government orders easier to implement, the Provincial Government simultaneously transferred all county magistrates in Sichuan, so that the county magistrate of area A was transferred to area B, and the county magistrate of area B was transferred to area C. In this way, the past malpractices of separation and isolation have been almost completely eliminated. Therefore, this first point of unifying Sichuan has already been fully achieved.

Reducing the People's Burden Second, reducing the people's burden. In the past, with the formation of the defense zone system, the collection of taxes in each military region was not only unlimited, but also lacked standards. In severe cases, taxes were collected ten times a year, and at least six or seven times in others. After the establishment of the new Provincial Government, it felt that the people's burden was too heavy and urgently wanted to find ways to reduce it to alleviate the people's difficulties. However, the situation at that time was special. There were hundreds of thousands of troops in Sichuan, and military expenses were huge, and the cost of suppressing bandits was particularly urgent, so it was still set at four levies a year. But looking back at the 24th year of the Republic, the actual burden on the people was more than that. First, because the recovery of the defense zones started from March 1, there were many pre-collected funds from the previous armies. Second, the construction of blockhouses, roads, etc., was stipulated by the headquarters as not requiring additional grain taxes. However, the situation in each county was different. In order to equalize the burden, there was no alternative but to add a little to the grain tax to meet the urgent needs. Because of these two reasons, when it comes to reducing the people's burden, we have not achieved it. Only in the possible scope, we have done things for the benefit of the people, such as implementing a single tax system, reducing tax rates, and abolishing checkpoints in various places to reduce the trouble for people traveling, which is still somewhat satisfactory.

Construction Projects Third, building a new Sichuan. The previous situation in Sichuan was extremely chaotic, and its vitality was greatly damaged. When it comes to building a new Sichuan, it is a very difficult thing, especially not something that can be done in a short time. Rather than chanting high-sounding slogans about some multi-year plan, it is better to practically achieve a few results. Therefore, within the political program implemented in the 24th year of the Republic, the construction items are all those that we can actually do. When drafting the program, the headquarters had not yet stipulated the amount of funding. Later, due to the expansion of military expenses, income and expenditure were not easy to match. The total administrative expenses of the province were stipulated to be 12 million yuan for the whole year. Various undertakings were limited by funding and could not be fully developed. In addition, the extension of the military affairs of suppressing bandits later led to various new undertakings failing to reach our expected level.

Work of Various Departments The work of various departments and offices in the past year has also achieved a lot. In terms of civil affairs, such as dividing the province into eighteen administrative inspector districts, and the county government's abolition of bureaus and reorganization into sections, the establishment of district offices, etc., have all been realized one after another. In addition, in order to cultivate grassroots talents for county administration, a training institute for county administrative personnel was specially established. There have been two sessions, and the number of graduates has exceeded 600. Land administration is also being prepared. Most of the other undertakings are also being planned and implemented, and will be implemented one by one in the near future. In terms of finance, such as the division of national and local taxes, the reorganization of old debts, the elimination of the long-standing malpractices of land taxes, the recovery of land notes, the establishment of the Three Provinces Bank, and the abolition of excessive taxes, judging from the implementation of the political program, it can be regarded as achieving sixty to seventy percent. In terms of education, such as the determination of the province's education funding as 1.8 million yuan per year, the rectification of higher education, the abolition of overlapping departments, the strengthening of military training and children's training, the verification of school teachers, and the promotion of free education, all these are efforts to restore the atmosphere and cultivate real talents. In terms of construction, such as the major repair of Dujiangyan, the opening of the Sichuan-Guizhou and Sichuan-Shaanxi highways, and the construction of the Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Hubei roads, all are constructed from the perspective of production. Recently, the Provincial Government and the Ministry of Railways have been working together to plan the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway. Today's Sichuan, when it comes to construction, not only focuses on development, but also needs to take national defense into consideration.

In terms of Security In terms of security, after the establishment of the Security Department, the first priority was to eliminate long-standing malpractices, reorganize the province's local militias into 412 security companies, and there were also proper regulations on funding, which must not be added arbitrarily. In addition, the establishment of a training class for security team cadres in the province, and the holding of training classes for county magistrates and training classes for strong men team cadres in various districts, are all actively underway.

Changing the Atmosphere Finally, there is still something to say to all colleagues. The common problem of Chinese people is that they are unwilling to do things themselves, but they are jealous of others doing things. This is a very bad phenomenon. I think many things are not afraid of being monopolized, but afraid of not being done. In the future, when we want to comment on something or criticize someone, we must obtain definite facts before drawing conclusions. Rumors and speculations are already bad when they come from ordinary people, and even more so when they come from civil servants. Chairman Liu always expects his colleagues to change the atmosphere, and hopes that his colleagues will pay more attention, so as not to lose their status as civil servants and can set an example for others.

The situation of the Sichuan Provincial Government's implementation of new policies in the past year as described in Deng's speech is all factual. In just one year, such achievements have been made, and the progress is not insignificant. This is indeed due to the supervision of the central authorities, and the efforts and progress of the Sichuan authorities are also commendable. (National News Agency, 12th)

Regulations of Jin Province: Measures for Reviving Agriculture and Commerce 72

Establishing a Rural Relief Bureau to Train Merchants Inside and Outside the Province

Taiyuan Dispatch: The stagnation of finance and the bankruptcy of the rural economy in Jin Province have always been a concern of the authorities. In addition to the joint establishment of a fully-prepared real goods reserve by the four provincial banks and firms to purchase agricultural products to ease the situation, a provincial rural relief bureau has recently been established. Wang Xiang, concurrently the commissioner of the Provincial Committee and the Department of Construction, recently resigned from his position as commissioner to devote himself to the affairs of the Rural Relief Bureau. The authorities have also convened a provincial cotton industry conference in recent days to stipulate promotion methods and compel people to plant cotton. It is reported that Yan Xishan intends to simultaneously advance the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce. On the morning of the 12th, Yan specially convened related personnel from the financial and industrial sectors at the Suiyuan Headquarters to discuss the progress. The following are the resolutions recorded:

Agent Merchants Convenience Measures In order to universally relieve the rural areas of this province, the government previously sent personnel to various remote counties to purchase agricultural products, so that the economic activities of the province tend to balance and development. Now, in order to facilitate merchants, each merchant is allowed to apply for agency. As for the agency affairs of merchants, in addition to handling in accordance with the agency regulations, the director of the Economic Control Office, Zhang Zhijie, is specially designated to convene the grain merchants in this city, and the assistant manager of the Reserve, Hao Qingzhao, is designated to convene the silver and money industry in this city to study the convenience measures for agency according to the actual local situation. It is decided that each agent merchant will be gradually established in the short term. As for the agent merchants in other counties, many have been approved.

Promote Production Comprehensive Management The Rural Relief Bureau established in this province is managed in a comprehensive manner in the latest way. The primary task is to revive the rural economy and provide as much support and promotion as possible for agricultural and industrial products in various counties. In the future, the Rural Relief Bureau, the Real Goods Reserve, and the Produce Trading Company will cooperate. In addition to the director, Wang Xiang, also serving as the manager of the Reserve, the internal personnel of the Bureau will be concurrently managed by the personnel of the Real Goods Reserve. The organizational methods and work progress plan will be formulated in detail after Wang takes office.

Xue and Kong Assigned to Shaanxi and Gansu Regarding the revival of the province's overseas commerce, it was discussed in detail last week, and the issue was continued to be discussed on the morning of the 12th. It is planned to convene unemployed merchants as soon as possible for centralized training. In the northwest provinces such as Qinghai, Shaanxi, Ningxia, Xinjiang, etc., merchants from this province still account for the majority. Xue Xiuqing (father of Xue Dubi) and Kong Fan, etc., who have excellent knowledge and rich experience, are specially requested to go to these provinces to guide and impart new knowledge. The training methods have now been formulated and will be implemented after detailed review.

Ten Counties Dispatch Personnel to Reorganize Public Property To reorganize the province's overseas public property such as guild halls and land, the Chamber of Commerce is urged to convene merchants from various counties in the province who are familiar with the outside world to come to the province to discuss methods. It is now stipulated that each of the ten counties in the Central Route will send one representative to the province to form a reorganization committee, and Xue Xiuqing and Kong Fan are requested to convene the local merchants to handle the matter when they go to the various counties to guide the merchants. The income after the reorganization will be entirely used to revive the province's overseas commerce.

Regulating People's Food Milling Flour by Oneself In order to regulate people's food and balance grain prices, it was previously decided that the Reserve would mill flour by itself. A proper method has been agreed upon with Jin Feng Electric Light and two manufacturers. Jin Feng Company signed a contract on the 9th, and the Electric Light Company also signed on the 12th. For the flour milling method, Jin Feng Company has a total of five machines, which can grind 1,500 shi of wheat per day and produce more than 4,000 bags of flour. The machines that were previously stopped will be opened for grinding in the future, and the Northwest Electric Plant will supply electricity. It is also stipulated that in order to maintain the operation of the plant, the first half of each month will be for the Reserve to grind flour, and the second half of the month will be for the stone mill to grind flour. The Reserve has recently hired many flour milling technicians from Shanghai, who can start grinding within days. As for the Electric Light Company, it can grind 600 shi of wheat per day and produce 1,500 bags of flour, which is stipulated for the whole month. After the flour is produced, it will be sold at the most balanced price. Yan Xishan also personally instructed the personnel of the Reserve that in order to maintain the people's food, there should be no profit-making behavior. (February 12)

Jiangxi Province Stipulates This Year as the Year of Water Conservancy Construction 73

The Province is Divided into Eight Major Regions, with Both Flood and Drought Prevention Advancing

Nanchang Dispatch: The Jiangxi Provincial Government now takes the revitalization of rural areas as the center of politics, and the revitalization of rural areas takes water conservancy construction as the only basic work. Therefore, the Provincial Government has specifically designated this year as the Year of Water Conservancy Construction. The construction plan has long divided the province into eight major regions, and the regional affairs are presided over by the Water Conservancy Bureau in conjunction with the administrative commissioners and county magistrates. All the rivers of the Gan River, Fu River, Rao River, Xin River, Xiu River, Yuan River, and Rui River, the middle and lower reaches will engage in embankment reinforcement, river dredging, and gate construction, and the upper reaches will engage in tree planting, canal opening, and well digging, one for flood prevention and the other for drought prevention, so as to advance on both sides. In addition to the severely affected areas such as northern Jiangxi using work as relief, the above projects are all conscripted labor. On average, all county Baojia strong men must serve for five to fifteen days. The first and second phases of conscripted labor in Fengcheng, Linchuan, and other counties have been implemented in order, and the main embankments of the rivers have been renewed. In terms of tree planting, all barren mountains, wasteland, and both sides of the roads are planted with trees. The seedlings are supplied by the Agricultural Institute, various water conservancy districts, various administrative regions, and even the nurseries of various counties and districts. The public officials in this city will perform labor service and plant trees on a regular basis in Qingyunpu. (February 10)

Anhui Finance Department Rectifies Land Deed and Other Taxes 74

More Commissioners Appointed as Heads of Land Deed Tax Bureaus

Wuhu Dispatch: In order to adjust the tax revenue of the province, the Anhui Finance Department is now determined to thoroughly improve local taxes and deed taxes. Regarding local taxes, the counties that have reported tax amounts, except for those that have exceeded the ratio or have sufficient ratio, are allowed to collect as before. Those with a large shortfall will be supervised and urged to re-examine them uniformly. All stores that have underreported, omitted, or reopened in the previous year will be verified on the spot and the ratio will be increased. Regarding deed taxes, during the period when the county government handled the matter, the annual income only reached two or thirty percent according to the ratio. Since the establishment of the office for reorganization in the 23rd year of the Republic, although the ratio has not yet been fully collected, it has actually exceeded the annual budget by more than one time. If the reorganization can be continued extensively, the annual million ratio will not be difficult to collect. This is also one of the major income sources of the provincial treasury. In addition to complying with Article 7, Paragraph 1 of the outline of the county government's abolition of bureaus and reorganization of sections promulgated by the chairman's headquarters, the Finance Department has specially reported that special bureaus will still be set up to collect taxes, and will also work with the Deed Tax Reorganization Office to replace those who have not handled the affairs of the county bureaus well in order to reorganize them. The newly appointed ones include Huang Zizhong, head of the Huaining Local Tax Bureau, Liu Xi of Lingbi, Tan Bing of Guoyang, Yu Qijun, head of the Huaining Deed Tax Bureau, Tang Ying of Tongcheng, Liu Ou of Chuxian, Huang Shengwu of Tianchang, Wang Jingwen of Lai'an, Wu Yulin of Xuyi, Guang Yingyuan of Linquan, and Sun Jingfang of Jiashan. Now many of them have taken up new positions and are implementing reorganization in accordance with the plans of the Finance Department. (February 15)

Registration Period for Smokers to Reform Themselves in Jiangsu Province Expires 75

—Total Investigation Starts on the 16th—

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The general registration of smokers in Jiangsu Province to reform themselves was uniformly announced to be closed on the 15th. The total number of registered smokers reached 70,000 by the 10th of this month. Statistics show that it will not be less than 80,000 by the 15th. From the 16th, the general investigation of drug offenders will begin. If private smokers are found thereafter, they will be punished with extremely severe crimes. The Department of Civil Affairs yesterday issued a strict order to the counties, saying, "This province has resolutely banned smoking for a long time. Since the implementation of the phased rehabilitation method, fearing that smokers are accustomed to long-standing habits and still have a fluke mentality, a mandatory registration has been implemented. Considering that smokers traveling abroad may not fully understand the smoking ban laws and regulations of this province, they are given a supplementary registration. Those who are stubborn and unrepentant will eventually be brought to justice. Before the implementation of the smoking ban and punishment regulations in this province, the principle of no punishment before the sentence and not punishing those who have not been educated is still followed. A self-surrender regulation for smokers has been formulated. All smokers who surrender to the local smoking ban authorities will be leniently exempted from punishment and given rehabilitation. The government is considerate and compassionate to these people who have fallen into the black book, and it is not to the point. They are expected to repent and return on their own, and it is not inappropriate to expect them to turn around. Although there have been tens of millions of people who have quit or are being rehabilitated and forcibly rehabilitated for a year, and in remote areas, ignorant people may not have heard of it or may have a contemptuous attitude, and there are still many places. Law enforcement is certainly unforgivable, and the original situation is still commendable. Therefore, a general investigation method for drug offenders has been stipulated, and the Baojia organization of this province has been used to hold the Baojia chiefs of the district and township responsible for the general investigation in order to thoroughly eliminate it. One month before the implementation of the general investigation, smokers who are indeed repentant may apply for self-renewal registration after proof to avoid punishment, receive a certificate for rehabilitation, and give them the last way to reform themselves. It should be known that the government's compassion and consideration for smokers is not hesitate to be repeated again and again, just to enable all the addicted and helpless smokers in the province to get rid of drug abuse, not to be hesitant and hesitant to those who are foolish and fearless of the law. Now that the period for self-renewal registration has expired, the government has done everything possible to give smokers who have not yet registered and received rehabilitation the opportunity to repent and renew themselves. From now on, only strict investigation and law enforcement will follow. It is hoped that the people who are suffering from drug addiction will be punished for the tragedy of destroying the country and destroying the species, and internally fear the worry of breaking up the family and losing their lives. They will uphold the government's original intention of implementing the policy and strive for their own self-reliance and self-improvement. They will quickly make a decision and quickly pull themselves together so that the number of smokers in the prison population will decrease day by day, and the drug offenders who are executed will not be recorded in the system. This is the government's original intention to eliminate drug abuse, and it is also the basis for the country and nation to strengthen and stand on its own. Each should think carefully and not make mistakes again. I hope that the county magistrate will give a kind announcement and make it known to all."

Qu Senlin of Qufu Village, Tianma Mountain, Fourth District, Songjiang County, is suspected of selling opium. Wuxi 78

The Deyuan Road Starts Construction

This county is holding labor service for public officials, teachers, and students, with the construction of Deyuan Road as the central task. Under the leadership of County Magistrate Long Tiyao and Construction Bureau Chief Zhang Fulin, 1,350 participants held a groundbreaking ceremony. In the early stage, the Construction Bureau sent personnel to divide the road into small sections, draw gray lines, and nail center stakes. Each section was marked with a flag to indicate it, and the road surface was stipulated to be 9 meters, the soil slope was 1:1.5, that is, 1 meter high and 1.5 meters horizontal, the soil ditch was 2 meters away from the roadside, and each person worked on 1 cubic meter of earthwork per day. Yesterday (16th) morning at 8:00 AM, 143 soldiers from the 6th Battalion of the Security Corps, led by Deputy Captain Shen, went to work on the road and were quite serious. They rested at 12:00 noon and continued to work at 2:00 PM until 5:00 PM. On the school side, it is scheduled to start construction on the 23rd of this month. The Construction Bureau sent technicians Xu Chuzhen and Wang Fengxiang to guide them. In addition, the street brick road and houses in Zhenyingdao Lane, from Chong'an Temple to Ximen Bridge, have been completely demolished. Hongmaosheng Meat Shop in Xiqiaopu has also been taken in. The remaining households that have not been demolished are limited to demolition by the end of February. Once everything is in place, road construction can begin. In the future, the road can be connected to Deyuan Road and reach Kaiyuan Road. In addition, the reconstruction of the Tingzi Bridge in the East Gate into a cement bridge can also begin in the near future.

The Adjudication Officer's Case of Malfeasance is Released on Bail

The former adjudication officers of the Jiangyin County Government, Zhou Xiang and Shi Wending, were suspected of accepting bribes and malfeasance. The Higher Court designated the local court of this county to hear the case and detained Zhou and Shi. After Zhou and Shi were imprisoned, they were sent to the Pure Benevolence Sanatorium and two hospitals for treatment because they were seriously ill. The forensic doctors were sent to guard them in turns. The inside story of the case has been slightly revealed after several interrogations by the court. The prosecutor Shen recently signed and submitted the detained related persons Chen Yipeng and Yuan Quanmei to the court and sent them back to the Jiangyin County Government for trial. Zhou and Shi were also brought to the court and released on bail separately. It was ordered that Zhou Xiang pay 2,000 yuan in cash and 2,000 yuan in written guarantee. At that time, 2,000 yuan in cash had been sent to the court, but it was difficult to find a store for the 2,000 yuan written guarantee. Only three ordinary stores were found, but they could not be released on bail and were still sent to the hospital for treatment. Shi Wending's share was 1,000 yuan each for cash and written guarantee, approximately 500 yuan in cash and 2,000 yuan in written guarantee, and he is expected to be released on bail today (17th).

The Issue of Silver Usage in the Silverware Industry

Regarding the issue of silver usage in the silverware industry in this county, the County Chamber of Commerce requested the Ministry of Finance in December last year to make changes to the regulations on the management of silver usage for silver products. After the telegram was sent, the Ministry approved it, roughly stating that the regulations on silver usage for silver products stipulate that chemistry should be used as raw material, and that the amount of pure silver contained in those that must be made of pure silver should not exceed 30% to show restrictions. After receiving the approval, the Chamber of Commerce immediately transferred it to the Gold and Silver Industry Association for notification. After receiving the letter, the Association immediately called a special meeting of all members, stating that the manufacture of silver products and silver ornaments, in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry, requires coordination and is difficult to manufacture. Therefore, all members were convened to hold a special meeting. Since the silverware industry in Shanghai also scheduled a meeting on the 23rd of this month, they unanimously called for. Zhang Shanqing, Cheng Fangren, and Ma Guanghui were selected to attend the meeting in Shanghai. If necessary, representatives must also be sent to Beijing to petition in order to achieve the purpose of changing the regulations on the management of silver usage for silver products.

Jiaxing 79

Nanhui Rice Shop Robbed

On the night of the 11th, six families, including Sheng Langchun and Sheng Bujin, in Shengjialangxia, north of Jiaxing, were robbed and suffered no goods. They are reporting and requesting a survey to investigate the thieves. Around half an hour before the morning of the 15th, more than ten robbers suddenly came to the Mingsheng Rice Shop in Xishi, Nanhui Town, north of Jiaxing. They dug into the door and first scared the shop assistants Fei Shiying and the watchman, and prohibited them from making a sound. The thieves who were guarding the door twisted the night watchman Jiangbei Asan. Zhang Renxiang, the accountant, heard the sound and hid, but forgot to take the leather suitcase next to his pillow, which was stolen, containing more than 40 yuan in paper money. Then they used tools to dig open the foreign box in the shop, which contained more than 600 yuan in paper money, all of which were stolen. Finally, they packed more than ten bags of copper coins into another bag and fled towards the Chaiquan Port. After the thieves left, the town police station was reported to dispatch police to pursue them, but the thieves had gone far and were not caught.

Zhenjiang 80

Crowds of Visitors to the Cultural Relics Exhibition

The cultural relics exhibition hosted by the Provincial Library officially began at 1:00 PM on the 15th. In order to avoid crowding, the library specially distributed admission tickets in advance, divided into regular tickets and designated date tickets. In addition to a portion directly distributed by the library, the rest were distributed by the Central Bookstore Zhenjiang Bookstore, Dahua Hotel, Wusan Library, and other places. The exhibition time is from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM. Yesterday was the first day of the exhibition, and the number of visitors was extremely enthusiastic, estimated to be no less than a thousand people. Each exhibition room in the library was staffed with receptionists. If the audience did not understand, there were ancient dictionaries on the wall. Jinshi was displayed in the cabinets in the south room, which was the most precious. Among them were several pieces of Jiading bamboo carving, one of which was "Zhu He's Pen Sea." Zhu He was the ancestor of Jiading bamboo carving, and few of his extant works are seen. This piece can be called a masterpiece and is said to be worth more than 100,000 yuan. One is Shen Lian's "Peach Boat." Shen Lian is also a famous bamboo carver in Jiading. The boat was hand-carved by him with exquisite knife skills and is also of high value. The rest, such as Bai Yangshanren's "Aloeswood Mountain", are all rare and excellent works. The next is pottery, most of which is lent by Chu Nanzhi, a Yixing scholar. Among them is a "Gongchun Skinny Pot," which is a pottery from Yixing. Only this one exists in China. Once a British person was willing to cut it off for 20,000 yuan, but he was rejected. It can be imagined how much Chu valued this pot. Other utensils, such as Saint Si's pottery cup, are also extremely valuable. The calligraphy and paintings are particularly beautiful, with countless works to admire. Tang Yin Qiu Shizhou's collaboration of ladies, Zheng Banqiao's ink orchids, etc., are the best of the best. The two large rooms and four small rooms downstairs are all calligraphy and paintings by modern celebrities, as well as modern printed painting albums, edition pieces, the first issues of various magazines, and newspapers from various countries.

Nantong 81

Famous Lawyer Sentenced to Imprisonment

Litigation is most prevalent in counties under Tongzhou jurisdiction. The Nantong District Commissioner's Office, in order to rectify local customs, ordered all counties to implement a movement to reduce litigation and strictly apprehend lawyers. Guan Celiu, a famous lawyer in Nantong, was arrested by the Public Security Bureau. Six manuscript books were found, containing over a thousand civil, criminal, and administrative cases he had handled. He was handed over to the court. On the 14th, the Criminal Court concluded the trial and announced the sentence: Guan Celiu, intending to profit, made it his regular business to solicit litigation for others and was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment.

Special Report

Biological Survey and Research Undertakings That China Urgently Needs to Develop (Continued) 82

— Hu Xiansu

Research on Insecticides

Since research on pest control has gradually progressed, research on insecticides has attracted attention. In various countries in Europe and America, lead arsenate, Paris green, potassium cyanide, and other chemicals are commonly used. Under the circumstances of underdeveloped industry and low prices of agricultural products in China, it is not economical to use industrially manufactured insecticides purchased from foreign countries. Therefore, it is necessary to research domestic plant insecticides. In recent years, the use of croton powder for insect control by the Zhejiang Provincial Bureau of Entomology has shown significant effectiveness. However, there are many domestic plants that can be used as insecticides, but it is easier to achieve results if biological research institutions undertake this work. In the future, as hygiene undertakings progress, even for eliminating mosquitoes, domestic insecticides will need to be utilized.

Research on Other Economic Plants

In addition to the above-listed economic plants, there are many other economic plants that need to be researched, such as extracting iodine from seaweed, bacterial culture media, forage grass, cork, legumes, green manure, leguminous shrubs in tea gardens, tannin raw materials, rubber sources other than rubber trees, honey plants, and so on, which are too numerous to mention individually. The existing Central Agricultural Experiment Station lacks the manpower and resources to research these, and the government should entrust and subsidize biological research institutions to actively investigate and research them.

Research on Plant Diseases

Besides pests, plant diseases are caused by pathogens. The extent of damage caused by the two is difficult to compare. For example, the loss of wheat due to wheat rust is enormous. Potato blight once caused the Great Famine in Ireland. The chestnut blight in the United States will completely exterminate the American chestnut. White pine blister rust has also made it almost impossible to plant this most valuable forest tree in the eastern United States. The fungal diseases of agricultural and forestry products in China have not yet been extensively investigated and studied, and this research must start from the fundamental mycology aspect of plant pathology. Currently, two or three biological research institutions are working hard on preliminary research, and it is necessary to support and encourage them so that they can progress quickly.

Research on Fermentation Bacteria and Bacteria

Fermentation bacteria and bacteria are greatly related to the national economy and people's livelihood. Pasteur's research results were enough to repay France's reparations to Germany after the Franco-Prussian War with surplus. The study of soil bacteria is of great importance to agriculture. The alcohol industry, beet sugar industry, wine-making industry, black tea manufacturing, soy sauce manufacturing, etc., are all related to the study of fermentation bacteria and bacteria. Our nation is the most capable of utilizing fermentation bacteria and bacteria without scientific methods. The manufacturing of soy sauce, fermented bean curd, rice noodles, red noodles, and preserved eggs are all unique techniques of our nation, unknown to European and American nations. In modern times, only Japan has made efforts to study fermentation organisms using scientific methods. Our country should catch up and vigorously engage in this research, as its impact on the national economy and people's livelihood is incalculable.

Survey and Research of Aquatic Organisms

The coastline of China, from Bohai Bay in the north to Guangzhou Bay in the south, spans thousands of miles from the north temperate zone to the tropics. The abundance of aquatic products is self-evident. And the consumption of aquatic food by the Chinese people is also higher than that of other nations. Every year, there is a large import surplus of aquatic products from Japan. In the past, there was no shortage of people studying aquatic science, but they lacked in-depth research on the taxonomy of aquatic animals and plants. Therefore, although fisheries schools have been established over the years, they have not benefited China's fishery industry at all. Not only have they failed to increase the production of aquatic products with the results of ecological research, but also the survey of China's aquatic products cannot be carried out. Furthermore, the problem of iodine production, which is related to medicine and national defense, has not been addressed because there are no experts in seaweed research. Moreover, China is famous for its fish farming industry, but the types of fish raised are limited. If scientific research is added, the types of fish that can be raised should be more than this. In addition, the consumption of kelp in our country is very high every year, and all of it comes from Japan. However, the Japanese have already transplanted kelp in the Dalian area with excellent results. On other coasts of our country, it may also be possible to try transplanting this type of seaweed. Moreover, for the prevention and control of mosquitoes, special types of fish that prey on mosquito larvae in the water are now mostly cultivated. This type of research is of great importance to hygiene. For example, the miasma of Yunnan and Guangdong has been proven to be malignant malaria. And when severe malaria is prevalent, it often leads to the complete death of the population of the entire county. In the future, if one wants to develop the tropical border areas, one must start by controlling mosquitoes. It is said that the fall of the Roman Empire was due to malaria, and the extinction of the Maya culture in Central America was also due to yellow fever mosquitoes. Today, in the vicinity of Rome, Italy, mosquitoes are controlled by transplanting fish. This type of research is also an urgent matter of government today. Fortunately, there are many aquatic zoologists in the country, and there are also experts in seaweed research. Currently, the Institute of Zoology and Botany of the Academia Sinica has begun large-scale research on oceanography and the survey of aquatic products. The government should fully support it and encourage other biological research institutions to engage in this research. (To be continued)

Local News

Unveiling Ceremony Held Yesterday Morning 83

Mayor Unveiled, Hu Yunqiu Reported on Preparations, Wang Xiaolai and Others Gave Speeches, City Lowered Flag

The Tomb of Nameless Heroes in Miaohang held its unveiling ceremony at ten o'clock yesterday morning. The mayor unveiled the tomb, and the city lowered its flag. Details are as follows:

Attendees The attendees included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government Yu Hongjun, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession Wang Xiaolai, as well as Yu Qiaqing, Kui Yanfang, Hu Yunqiu, Mao Heyuan, Li Dachao, and representatives from agricultural, industrial, commercial, and academic circles, totaling over 400 people. The venue and along the route were protected and maintained by over 200 security team members, police officers, and Boy Scouts from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Venue Arrangement The venue was in Miaohang. The organizers stipulated that all participants must wear badges, so badges were checked at the entrance of the China Leprosy Hospital and the entrance to the venue. Those without badges could purchase them. An altar was set up in front of the tomb, with the Party and National flags and a portrait of Sun Yat-sen placed on it, along with flowers. In the center of the tomb, a memorial tablet for the soldiers who died in the January 28th Incident was hung, with red silk and black characters, and flower wreaths and baskets presented by various sectors were lined up.

Mayor Unveiled The conference was chaired by Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, and Zhang Gongquan. After the formalities, the mayor first cut the red silk covering the tomb door with silver scissors, opening the tomb door. The unveiling ceremony was completed. The mayor, accompanied by the presidium, went inside for a week's tour, and then returned to the original place. Yu Qiaqing reported that, ladies and gentlemen, today is the unveiling ceremony of the tomb of the soldiers who died in the January 28th Incident. All sectors have come from afar to participate, which proves the patriotism of all sectors towards the soldiers. The cloudy and rainy weather proves that even the heavens are weeping. We are here today to participate in the unveiling ceremony, and we should inherit the legacy of the martyrs so as not to be ashamed of them.

Preparations Next, Hu Yunqiu reported on the preparations, saying, ladies and gentlemen, you are probably well aware of the initiation of the construction of the Tomb of Nameless Heroes. This tomb project began after the ceasefire and has been under construction for four years. It was originally planned to be unveiled on the fourth anniversary of the January 28th Incident, but due to the internal construction, it was only able to be held today. The founding committee believes that the construction of this tomb is an expression of national spirit and should not be overly simple. It is hoped that all sectors will donate more to express the admiration of the masses. In the future, for permanent preservation, it will be handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Government for management.

Mayor's Speech Then, Mayor Wu gave a speech, saying that the Tomb of Nameless Heroes is the resting place for heroes who sacrificed for the nation. Because their names are unknown, they are named with the words "Nameless" to commemorate the glorious deeds of the nation. Wang Xiaolai followed with a speech, briefly stating that we, as businessmen, should organize in the form of unlimited companies with unlimited spirit, promote the inherent spirit of the nation, and strive for the strength of the nation.

Zhang's Speech Zhang Zhizhong gave a speech, saying that he was one of those who personally experienced the January 28th battle, so he came from Beijing to participate in the unveiling of the Tomb of Nameless Heroes. In that battle, in Miaohang alone, a regiment of people sacrificed in the artillery fire, which shows the intensity of the battle. Although I am here today to participate and gather with people from Shanghai in front of the Tomb of Heroes, I feel deeply ashamed that even in the midst of the fierce war, I failed to sacrifice for the country and the people. After the speech, he shouted "Long live the Republic of China, long live the Kuomintang of China, and may the spirit of the nameless heroes never die!" and then the ceremony ended.

Half-Mast for Mourning The Vice President of the Executive Yuan sent a couplet to the Tomb of Nameless Heroes. In addition, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, former Commander of the Fifth Army Zhang Zhizhong, former Garrison Commander of Songhu Dai Ji, former Commander of the 88th Division Yu Jishi, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Yu Zuoting, China Flying Society, China Aviation Association, and others sent flower baskets and wreaths. The entire city lowered its flags to mourn.

A Glimpse of the Tomb Road The Tomb of Nameless Heroes is located in the central district of Miaohang Town, covering an area of over 50 acres. The entire outline is shaped like a sword, with the main part of the tomb hall at the end of the sword handle. The main road in the middle is the body of the sword. The flag pole road that crosses the main road is parallel to the front of the tomb hall, which is the image of the sword guard. The entire architectural style is simple and solid, decorated with Chinese floral carvings, quiet and elegant. The tomb hall is a slightly rectangular three-dimensional building, standing on a large stone platform that is 128 feet wide and 110 feet deep. There are 15 stone steps on the four sides of the platform, divided into three layers. The front is about 30 feet wide. There is a semi-circular pit in the hall, with a stone sarcophagus in the middle, which is the place to bury the remains of the nameless heroes and soldiers who died. A stone tablet stands at the rear, with a large red flag bearing the inscription "Spirits of the Soldiers Who Died in the January 28th Incident". Those who come to pay their respects will spontaneously generate a heart of admiration. The upper part of the tomb hall is adorned with the four characters "义薄云天" (Righteousness Piercing the Clouds), handwritten by Lin Sen, Chairman of the National Government. The stone tablet inside the hall has the six large characters "Tomb of Nameless Heroes". The entire project took two and a half years, designed by engineer Dong Dayou, and contracted by Jiuji Construction Factory for over 66,000 yuan. The nearby Sijing Temple is the temple from which Miaohang got its name. It was destroyed in the artillery fire of the January 28th Incident, and is still being rebuilt by the locals through fundraising, and has not yet been completed.

Wei and Li Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 84

Wei Carried Hu's Handwritten Letter to Beijing to Present to Chiang

Wei Daoming, former Minister of Judicial Administration, and Li Xiaosheng, member of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, took the postal ship Conte Verde from Hong Kong and arrived in Shanghai at around 7:00 yesterday morning, docking at the Zhaoshang North Wharf. Wang Sima, President of the Second Special District Court, and Liang Renjie, President of the High Court Branch, welcomed them. Wei and Li disembarked at around 8:30 and went to their residences to rest. Wei will go to Beijing today to report everything to President Chiang. Li will stay in Shanghai. Wei and Li met with reporters on the ship and made the following statements:

According to Wei Daoming, Mr. Hu Zhantang has decided to wait until the weather is warmer before going to Shanghai and then to Beijing. The only reason Mr. Hu delayed his trip north is that his health has not recovered. Mr. Hu suffered from climatic changes on his way back to China and was unwell. After returning to China, he suffered from two episodes of colds. Moreover, Mr. Hu's body is not suitable for cold weather. He previously lived abroad and moved from Germany to France for treatment for this reason. He has now decided to follow the doctor's advice and wait until the weather is warmer before setting off for the north. I am carrying a handwritten letter from Mr. Hu to President Chiang, which I will present in person in Beijing in the next day or two. The letter also states that he has decided to wait for spring to warm up before coming north. Mr. Wang Chonghui left Spain today on the North German Company's fast ship Scharnhorst No. 1 (according to North German Company, the ship is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on March 12). Wang will come directly to Shanghai. It has not yet been decided whether he will disembark when passing through Hong Kong.

According to Li Xiaosheng, Mr. Hu Zhantang had high blood pressure, which made him unwell, so he went abroad for treatment. He has now returned to China, and his blood pressure has indeed decreased, but his body has not fully recovered. After returning to China, he suffered from two episodes of colds, so he has not seen guests or gone out in recent days. The reports in the newspapers that Mr. Hu visited factories and met with relatives and friends were scheduled activities, but they have been cancelled due to his ill health. Mr. Hu has decided to stay in Guangdong for a short time and then return to Hong Kong. He will come north again when the weather is warmer. The rumor that he will go to Guangxi is not accurate. I came here purely to handle private affairs and do not plan to go to Beijing. As soon as I finish my work, I will return south. I have already submitted my resignation from the position of Minister of Personnel.

Carrying a Plan for Building Three Major Railways, He Will Go to Beijing to Consult the Ministry of Railways in the Next Few Days

Huadong News Agency reports that Li Xiangen, Director of the Southern Section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning with Wei Daoming and Li Xiaosheng on the Italian postal ship Conte Verde from Hong Kong. He is carrying a plan for building three major railways in Guangdong and Guangxi and plans to go to Beijing in the next few days to consult with the Ministry of Railways and then go to Hankou to inspect the Guangdong-Hankou Railway before returning to Guangdong via Hunan. Details are as follows:

Li told reporters on the ship that he came to Beijing to meet with Zhang Jia'ao, Minister of Railways, to request instructions on the construction of three major railways: Sanhe (from Sanshui in Guangdong to He County in Guangxi), Qin-Yong (from Qinzhou in Guangdong to Nanning in Guangxi), and Guang-Shan (from Guangzhou to Shantou). He plans to go to Beijing in the next few days to meet with Minister Zhang. After completing his official duties in Beijing, he will take a boat to Hankou to inspect the Guangdong-Hankou Railway and then return to Guangzhou via Hunan.

Regarding the funding for the three major railways to be built in Guangdong and Guangxi, after the Ministry of Railways approved the central government to issue railway public bonds, the amount of public bonds to be allocated to Guangdong and Guangxi is now being drafted by the ministry to allocate funds. The Ministry of Railways sent Xia Guangyu, a member of the Railway Design Institute, to Guangdong last month to discuss with the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities and inspect everything. Xia will also return north after completing his work. As for the three major railways, all engineering plans and budgets have also been finalized. Guangxi has established a preparatory office for the construction of the Sanhe Railway in Wuzhou. The situation is similar for the Qin-Yong Railway. Lin Yinhao, Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, has ordered He Qifeng, Director of the Construction Department, to work with me and Li Luchao and Wang Renkang, Directors of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Bureau. All of this is included in the construction plan, which I brought with me for Minister Zhang to consult and handle.
