Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange Announces Opening Today 87

Unified Bonds Have Not Been Printed, So Do Not Make New Transactions Temporarily, the Brokers' Association Resolved Two Remedial Measures

The Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange, after receiving the order from the Ministry of Finance, announced that it will open for trading today, but do not make new transactions temporarily. The Brokers' Association of the Exchange held a general meeting yesterday afternoon and resolved two measures to request the chairman for remedy. Details are as follows:

Announcing the Opening Today

Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange issued Announcement No. 22500 yesterday, stating that it received an order from the Ministry of Finance to open. The Ministry had previously sent personnel to work with the exchange supervisor to verify the reports submitted by the exchange, and after checking them one by one, it was found that there were no public officials or personnel of the Ministry engaging in speculation and manipulation. The exchange should be allowed to open as usual from the 17th of this month. However, the unified public bonds have not yet been printed, and the exchange of new and old bonds has not yet begun. The exchange should not make new transactions temporarily when it opens on the 17th to avoid obstacles during delivery. The order has been received, and the exchange will comply and open as usual on the 17th of this month. However, new transactions will be temporarily suspended. Spot transactions will also be temporarily suspended because new futures transactions are temporarily suspended. This is hereby announced.

Brokers Hold a General Meeting

The Brokers' Association of the exchange held a general meeting at 2:00 p.m. yesterday in the signing room downstairs in the exchange. All brokers, as well as President He Peiyuan, Vice Presidents Zhu Anfu and Qiu Lianggui, Directors Li Zisheng, Fu Weiyuan, Zhu Dingyi, Zhu Dajun, Liu Yunpan, and Ge Gengzu, attended. First, Chairman He Peiyuan read out the original letter from the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange to the Brokers' Association and reported the purpose of convening the general meeting. Then, the discussion began. The public resolved to comply with the order of the Ministry of Finance to open for trading, but requested to open new purchases and equalize market prices, and to cancel the submission of spot goods. These two points were entrusted to President He Peiyuan and two others to visit Zhang Weiru, Chairman of the Exchange, to request assistance. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 p.m. In the evening after the meeting, President He Peiyuan and two others visited Zhang Weiru, Chairman of the Exchange, to report on the meeting and request that the two remedial measures be resolved and forwarded to Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance, for review.

The Exchange Is Ready

In addition to announcing the opening today, the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange has prepared everything for the opening yesterday, such as repairing the red number lights used to announce prices. It is reported that the various treasury bills and public bonds to be traded today will temporarily use the old names, but no new transactions may be made. For example, the public bonds and treasury bills that were sold before the suspension may be bought back now, and the public bonds and treasury bills that were bought before may be sold now, entirely to clear the previous accounts. After the unified public bonds are printed and the exchange of new and old bonds is completed, trading will begin again. The exchange has made nameplates for various public bonds of A, B, C, D, and E types specified in the unified public bonds, such as the Reconstruction Public Bonds and the Unified Public Bonds. The opening date will be determined by the order of the Ministry.

Notice from National Trust and Credit Bank

The Savings Department of the National Trust and Credit Bank issued a notice to customers with treasury bill interest savings deposits, stating that the bank has been providing services to the public, including the custody of various treasury bills and the collection of interest savings deposits, and has received generous support and patronage from all sectors, for which it is deeply grateful. Now, in order to balance the treasury's income and expenditure and improve the financial organization, the Ministry of Finance has decided to issue 146 million yuan of unified public bonds in the 25th year of the Republic of China to exchange for various old bonds. Therefore, the bank's treasury bill interest deposit has ceased to exist. A public notice is hereby issued requesting all customers with treasury bill interest savings deposits to bring their original passbooks and the original seal left at the bank to retrieve the original treasury bills held in custody to clear the procedures. As for the previous interest savings deposits, the bank has a special fixed deposit savings account with the same nature and interest rate as the treasury bill interest savings deposit. Customers can continue to renew the deposit according to the original term, or convert it to other savings deposits. If you do not wish to continue to deposit and wish to withdraw, the bank will handle it according to the interest rate set for current and convenient savings deposits, depending on the length of the deposit period, and will provide special treatment to thank you for your patronage. It is hoped that all customers will consider this and come to negotiate as soon as possible.

The China Weight and Measures Association’s 7th Representative Congress Opens Yesterday Morning 90

Afternoon Session of the General Assembly

The 7th Representative Congress of the China National Bar Association was held yesterday (Sunday) at 9 a.m. at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society Hall on Route Père Robert, Avenue MacMahon, in the French Concession. In addition to all the representatives, all members of the Shanghai Bar Association's Executive and Supervisory Committees, the head of the General Assembly Secretariat, and representatives from various Party, government, legal, commercial, and organizational bodies in the city attended. A total of thirty-five motions were submitted by the representatives. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Outside the gate of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society, a tall archway of pine and cypress was erected, with the words "The 7th Representative Congress of the China National Bar Association" embedded in the center. The Party and national flags were hung, and the hall was decorated with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the flags of various nations. Apart from the platform for the presidium, the representatives were seated according to their assigned numbers. Representatives from various organizations and associations delivered speeches. The presidium responded. Music was played. The ceremony concluded and the meeting adjourned. The representatives gathered on the lawn behind the society to take a group photo as a memento.

Chairman's Speech

The presidium of the 7th Representative Congress of the Bar Association delivered an opening address, stating that the most important foundation of the association's work lies in strengthening the organic organization of the nation. According to our long-held observations, to strengthen the organic organization of the nation, it is enough that there is mutual love and understanding between the nation and its people, and among the people themselves. The association's movement for compensation for unjust imprisonments is a movement to promote mutual love between the nation and its people. The legal aid movement for the poor? Is a movement to awaken mutual love among the people, so as to form the most basic work of strengthening the organic organization of the country, with the upper and lower classes supporting each other and sharing the same virtues. Only lawyers can be good at using the law, and they can also eliminate the reasons that hinder the strengthening of the organic organization of the country in advance. Therefore, legal education, lawyer training, lawyer treatment, and various systems should be improved, and legal academics should be emphasized. Moreover, in the modern era when the free school of law has expanded from the field of civil law to the field of criminal law, lawyers must have excellent legal academics. However, in our country, even in the legal field, emphasis on legal exploration is not active enough, and the original lawyers only regard dull legal judgments as golden rules. How can this clarify the role of the law and eliminate the reasons that hinder the strengthening of the organic organization of the country? Therefore, the association also advocates the study of law. In short, the recent main work of the association, although divided into the movement for compensation for unjust imprisonments, the legal aid movement for the poor, and the movement to study law, is only one movement to strengthen the organic organization of the country. We are fortunate to have your wise counsel.

Zhang Yuanruo's Speech

Municipal Government Representative Zhang Yuanruo delivered a speech, saying, “Brothers, I am very honored to represent the Shanghai Municipal Government to attend this grand meeting today. All of you present are leaders in the legal field and specialized scholars. Although I am usually very interested in law and enthusiastically promote it, I always feel that my talents are lacking. Now I just want to contribute a few superficial opinions. China has a long history, a vast territory, and a large population, but why can't we strengthen the national organization? As for this phenomenon today, I think it is only because it lacks an element, which is law. Because the country lacks this political element, the foundation of society cannot be laid for long-term stability and security. We want to make society evolve, there is only one point, that is, to change the society from one without laws and unscientific to one with laws and scientific principles. However, in order to avoid becoming empty talk, we must strive to carry out this work in the future."

Tong Xingbai's Speech

City Party Representative Tong Xingbai delivered a speech, saying, "Representatives, today the China National Bar Association is holding its 7th National Representative Congress in Shanghai. I am very happy to represent the Shanghai City Party Department and attend this grand meeting. You have all come from afar. I represent the City Party Department to express my greetings to you. Since the transformation of China, various popular groups and organizations have sprung up like mushrooms, but many national organizations are always scattered. However, the organization and spirit of your association are very good and can be regarded as a model for the people. You are all famous legal experts. I believe that in the future, on the one hand, we should further improve the legal system itself, and on the other hand, we should also instill legal concepts into the people, so that the people can understand the law and develop law-abiding habits. Only by spreading legal knowledge to the people can the promotion of the legal system be effective."

Rules of Procedure

Rules of Procedure of the China National Bar Association, Chapter 1, General Provisions, Article 1, The meeting shall elect three to five persons from the representatives present to form the presidium, which shall preside in turn during the meeting, Article 2, The seating assignments of the representatives shall be determined by lottery, Article 3, The meeting time shall be from 9:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. daily. When necessary, the chairman may announce an extension or recess, Article 4, The meeting shall establish a secretariat to handle the preparation of the agenda, the organization of proposals, the recording of documents, and the accounting and general affairs of the association, Chapter 2, Meeting, Article 5, The meeting must have the number of persons stipulated in Article 13 of the articles of association to be able to convene, Article 6, All representatives speaking must first stand up and report their association name, Article 7, During the meeting, no two or more persons may speak at the same time. If this happens, the chairman shall designate the order in which they speak, Article 8, Representatives discussing proposals may not involve matters outside the scope, Article 9, All speakers shall not exceed five minutes each time, Article 10, Each person shall not speak more than three times on the same proposal, but this shall not apply to questions or answers, Article 11, During the meeting, the chairman may announce the end of debate, Article 12, During the meeting, if contradictions are found in the proposals or if they conflict with the current laws and regulations of the National Government, the proposer may request modification or withdrawal, Chapter 3, Proposals, Article 13, The meeting shall prepare meeting minutes, which shall be signed by the chairman, Article 14, The proposals of the meeting shall be limited to those stipulated in Article 1 of the articles of association, Article 15, All proposals must be submitted to the secretariat of the meeting before the meeting for inclusion in the agenda, but temporary motions must be seconded by representatives from more than one association before they can be submitted for discussion, Chapter 4, Review Committee, Article 16, The meeting shall establish various group review committees, which shall be organized by the chairman from designated representatives, Article 17, All proposals shall be submitted to the review committee for review according to their nature and category, but those that do not need to be submitted for review may be exempted from review, Article 18, The members of each group's review committee shall elect one director to manage the review of their review events, Article 19, The members of each group's review committee shall report the results of the review to the general assembly regarding the convening and organization of the committee for each case under review, and explain the reasons, Chapter 5, Voting, Article 21, The voting on proposals at this meeting shall be in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the articles of association, Article 22, When voting on proposals, the chairman shall announce the final result of the discussion on the case to the public and proceed by standing or raising hands. Once the proposal has been voted on, it shall not be discussed again. If the proposal is seconded and there is no objection, the voting procedure may be omitted, Article 23, Representatives shall sign their names in the attendance book when attending, Article 24, If a representative is unable to attend due to reasons, they shall explain the reasons and report to the presidium, Article 25, Representatives shall not leave the meeting at will after attending without the permission of the chairman, Chapter 7, Supplementary Provisions, Article 26, If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they shall be amended by the meeting.

The Jianghai Customs Patrol Vessels Employ National Crew Members 91

The Ministry of Finance Has Agreed to the Engineers' Association's Request

The China Marine Engineers Association previously stated that the employment of foreigners on customs patrol vessels was a serious hindrance to the national system and a waste of national funds. It submitted reasons to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation, requesting the employment of national crew members. It is heard that the Ministry of Finance has approved the request, and that the recruitment of foreign personnel will be stopped, and that as many nationals as possible will be hired. The Ministry of Finance's approval is recorded as follows: "Reply to the China Marine Engineers Association's submission regarding the request that the crew members of customs patrol vessels should be filled by nationals in order to recover interests and save national funds. I have read the submission. I have found that the customs authorities have already stopped recruiting foreign personnel. As for the employment of foreign drivers, this is because the Inspector General of Customs reported that it was difficult to find a sufficient number of suitable Chinese personnel at one time. Therefore, it was necessary to approve the establishment of a short-term contract system to temporarily employ a small number of foreign personnel to meet urgent needs. At the same time, many vacancies were still reserved to gradually recruit Chinese personnel. Recently, dozens of Chinese drivers have been hired, which has been reported to the Ministry's Customs Office by the Inspector General of Customs. In addition, all graduates of the maritime classes of the tax schools have also been assigned as reserve drivers and served on various patrol vessels. All of this shows the Ministry's intention to cultivate maritime talents and gradually replace foreign staff with Chinese personnel. Now that it is claimed that there are many specialized talents among the members of the association, they should apply for the position when the customs authorities recruit drivers or marine engineers. If they are qualified, they will be hired as much as possible. Please be informed of this reply."

British Australian Government Sends Personnel to Investigate the Actual Situation in Manchukuo

New Voice News Agency reported that the British Australian government has decided to send Dr. Clunies Ross from the Scientific and Industrial Research Association to the three northeastern provinces of China and Korea to investigate the economic situation in order to understand the actual situation since the puppet government took control of the eastern provinces. Mr. Ross has now completed his investigation and is on his way back to Australia. He passed through Shanghai and will take a ship to Hong Kong within days before returning to Australia.

江浙 Provinces to Appoint Committees to Survey Outer Sea Borders 92

Lu Yanghao of Jiangsu Submits Proposal to Civil Affairs Office, Strongly Arguing that the Shengsi Islands Should Not Be Assigned to Zhejiang's Jurisdiction

Following the proposal by Zhejiang Province to place the Shengsi Islands, located off the coast of Jiangsu Province, under Zhejiang's jurisdiction, gentry member Han Zishi from Jiangsu, as well as the Fishermen's Associations of thirty-one counties, have repeatedly expressed their opposition. Academic institutions in China's aquaculture sector have also unanimously voiced their opinions, opposing the change. Recently, the Ministry of Interior has ordered the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to appoint committees for a joint survey. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has already appointed Xu Zhen, Commissioner of Nantong, to participate in the survey. Lu Yanghao of Jiangsu visited the Civil Affairs Office a few days ago to present his views on the outer sea border survey to Director Yu, and stated that the Zhejiang proposal is a division of Jiangsu's territory, not a simple provincial border dispute, and is of great importance to Jiangsu's territorial rights and the livelihood of its fishing industry. The original proposal is excerpted below: It is understood that the division of the outer seas between Jiangsu and Zhejiang was determined as early as the 29th year of the Kangxi reign of the Qing Dynasty. Ye Ji and Yuan Erhuai, the left and right wing guerrilla commanders of the Dinghai Garrison in Zhejiang, and Ding Jichang and Guo Long, the left and right wing guerrilla commanders of the Suzhou Garrison in Jiangnan, jointly surveyed and erected a monument on Xiaoyang Mountain. The inscription on the monument stated the dividing mountain standard: "The maritime defense of Jiangnan is bounded by Maji Mountain. The ocean islands south of the foot of Maji Mountain are under the jurisdiction of Zhejiang Province. The maritime defense of Zhejiang is bounded by Dayang Mountain. The ocean islands north of the foot of Dayang Mountain are under the jurisdiction of Jiangnan Province. From west to east, the ocean surface mountains and islands are all based on these two mountains as the standard." The original monument still exists in the Laoshan Temple on Xiaoyang Mountain. It is verified that after this determination of the division of the outer seas between Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the boundary has been maintained for a long time without dispute. According to Zhejiang Province's local chronicles, such as the Zhejiang General Chronicle, the Kangxi Dinghai County Chronicle, the Guangxu Dinghai Subprefecture Chronicle, and the Republic of China Dinghai County Chronicle, the affiliation of the larger mountain islands in the outer seas are all recorded and can be used as reference. Also, Zhu Zhengyuan, a candidate for prefectural magistrate during the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, wrote "Illustrated Description of the Zhejiang Coast" and "Illustrated Description of the Jiangsu Coast," each with a volume of mountain and island tables. According to Zhu's table, the islands belonging to Dinghai match the mountain and island table listed in the Republic of China Dinghai County Chronicle. Therefore, the division of the outer seas between Jiangsu and Zhejiang has complete records that can be used for verification. The ocean surface has the clear boundaries of Maji and Dayang mountains, so there should be no disputes between the two provinces regarding the division of the outer seas. Unexpectedly, last year, the Ningbo, Dinghai, and Fenghua natives' associations in Shanghai of Zhejiang, and Zhao Cisheng, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner of the Fifth District, suddenly proposed assigning the Shengsi Islands to Zhejiang. Yanghao has successively written articles to address this and revealed the truth behind the proposed division. Now, I solemnly and sincerely declare to Your Excellency that the Zhejiang proposal is a division of Jiangsu's territory and cannot be regarded as a provincial border dispute. Previously, it was reported that the Executive Yuan had approved the assignment of the Shengsi Islands in Jiangsu to Zhejiang. Immediately, Mr. Han Zishi, Zhang Zhongren, Chen Taoyi, Tang Weizhi, Leng Yuqiu, Wang Dankui, and Yanghao sent separate telegrams to the Central Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior, strongly arguing against it. Soon, a reply telegram was received from the Ministry of Interior, acknowledging that the saying that the Executive Yuan had approved the assignment of the Shengsi Islands to Zhejiang was entirely fictitious. The case is currently under joint investigation by committees from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Now, hearing that Jiangsu Province has dispatched Commissioner Xu Zhen from the Nantong District to survey the border, I respectfully offer a few personal opinions before the survey, as detailed below: The division of the outer seas between Jiangsu and Zhejiang was originally undisputed. Now that the Ministry of Interior has ordered the governments of the two provinces to appoint committees for a joint survey, it is actually giving the two provinces an opportunity to establish a more obvious and definite provincial boundary. Xu Gong Mountain and the northern half of Dayang Mountain, which belong to Jiangsu, have long been occupied by Zhejiang. It is proposed that Your Excellency propose the recovery of these territories during the border demarcation to complete Jiangsu's territory. Before the Ministry of Interior promulgates the regulations for surveying provincial, municipal, and county administrative regions, if the boundary lines have long been clearly defined, have never been disputed, and there are no inconveniences, the original regional boundaries should be maintained. Article 4 of the Ministry of Interior's regulations for surveying provincial, municipal, and county boundaries has clear provisions. It is proposed that Your Excellency invoke these provisions and insist on the boundary established by the joint survey of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in the 29th year of Kangxi, permanently adhering to the original case. The Zhejiang natives' associations in Shanghai proposed assigning the Shengsi Islands to Zhejiang, using the pretext that "according to the reports from fellow natives residing on the islands of Shenshan and Sijiao." This was used as a disguise for expressing the opinions of the residents, but in reality, the residents of the islands had absolutely no such opinions beforehand, and strongly opposed it afterward. Declarations were published in the Shanghai Shenbao and the Jiangsu Research Monthly as statements. It is proposed that Your Excellency present the true intentions of the residents to the central government to expose Zhejiang's pretense. The vast ocean surface uses mountain islands as the standard for dividing the territory. What is even better than this is that the division of the boundary in the Kangxi era was based on the force of the Yangtze River and Qiantang River entering the sea, dividing the territory by the flow of shells. This is adopting the watershed of the Yangtze River and Qiantang River. It is truly a rational division of territory. If the people of Zhejiang insist on establishing a new boundary, it is proposed that Your Excellency propose using 30 degrees 30 minutes north latitude as the boundary for dividing the outer seas between Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The above are all reference opinions regarding the survey. As for the Shengsi Islands being the gateway to the Yangtze River, the protective screen for the six counties of Chongming, Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Fengxian, and Jinshan in Jiangsu, and Shenshan being Jiangsu's only fishing port, the islands belonging to Jiangsu are absolutely non-transferable territories. Your Excellency, as a Jiangsu native governing Jiangsu, has unparalleled insight. The various achievements in dispatching warships to protect fishing and strictly prohibiting all kinds of exploitative malpractices against fishermen over the years have long been known in the outer seas, so there is no need for Yanghao to add trivial details. The matter concerns Jiangsu's territorial rights and the livelihood of the fishing industry. Yanghao is not intelligent but offers a humble opinion, earnestly requesting Your Excellency to examine and verify it. Respectfully presented to Director Yu of the Civil Affairs Office, etc.

Ministry of Finance Reiterates Reward and Punishment Order for Confiscating Smuggled Silver 94

Official Receipt Should be Issued for Confiscated Smuggled Silver; Private Confiscation Will be Prosecuted as Embezzlement

The Ministry of Finance previously received confidential reports that police officers in various provinces and cities directly confiscated smuggled silver coins and silver items without issuing receipts, causing abuses. It immediately telegraphed to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering the police officers under their jurisdiction that if they seize smuggled silver coins or silver items, they should be handed over to the local Public Security Bureau for handling. If there are those who deliberately conceal or intend to evade taxes, the Public Security Bureau should forward them to the court for prosecution in accordance with the Emergency Punishment Law for Endangering the Republic of China. However, for silver coins and silver items directly confiscated by the Public Security Bureau, receipts should be issued as proof. Police officers must not confiscate privately, and violators should be prosecuted for embezzlement to prevent abuses. Furthermore, personnel who have contributed to the seizure of smuggled silver coins or silver items should be given bonuses. It is proposed to handle the distribution of bonuses in accordance with the revised Measures for Punishing and Rewarding the Seizure of Smuggled Silver Coins and Silver Items. After the confiscated silver coins or silver items are sent to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications for exchange into legal tender, the bonuses will be distributed according to the following rules: If the seizure is made independently by customs or military police agencies, the bonuses will be doubled in accordance with the customs' reward method for informants without connections, that is, 60% for extraordinary meritorious service and 40% for ordinary meritorious service. If the customs receive information from informants and seize the smuggled items with the assistance of military police agencies, the bonuses will be doubled in accordance with the customs' reward method for informants with connections. The military police and informants will each receive 40%, and customs officers will receive 20%. If military police agencies receive information from informants and seize the smuggled items, the informants will receive 60% of the bonus, and the military police will receive 40%. If the customs seize the smuggled items based on information from informants, the informants will receive 60% of the bonus, and the customs officers will receive 40%. If the customs seize the smuggled items with the assistance of military police, the military police will receive 50% of the bonus, and the customs officers will receive 50%.

Nanyang Inspection Delegation Requests Government to Appoint Delegation Leader 95

Departure to Develop Foreign Trade is Imminent; Overseas Chinese are Requested to Establish Agencies for Selling Domestic Goods

The Nanyang Commercial Inspection Delegation organized by the Shanghai Institute for the Development of Foreign Trade, sponsored by the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association, held a five-member board meeting the other day to discuss and decide on the number and duties of the delegation leader and deputy leader. Zhang Hui-kang attended the meeting. It was decided that the delegation should have one leader, two deputy leaders, one secretary, and one accountant. The leader and secretary will be appointed by the government and will be responsible for foreign affairs and public speaking. The deputy leaders and accountant will be publicly elected by the delegation members. The delegation members are divided into three categories: Category A, those who send personnel independently; Category B, those who jointly send personnel from several factories; and Category C, those who entrust agents. The delegation's tasks are divided into four categories: (1) Promotion, including soliciting agents, trading directly with stores, and contacting enthusiastic overseas Chinese to establish agencies for selling domestic goods; (2) Investigation, including investigating whether the goods from various factories meet local needs, comparing the prices and materials of goods from various factories with similar foreign goods, and investigating the local government's tax rates and restrictions on goods from various countries; (3) Promotion, including screening films brought by various factories and participating in domestic goods exhibitions; (4) Liaison, including contacting consulates and chambers of commerce, and enthusiastic overseas Chinese who are engaged in the domestic goods movement. As for the departure period, it was decided to depart in May of this year.

Mr. Pan Gongzhan Plans to Excavate Antiquities 96

Intends to Distribute Discovered Pottery Fragments in Sets, Storing Them in Various Counties as Excavation Samples

In recent years, more and more antiquities have been discovered in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Artifacts have been unearthed in Jinshan, Yan City, Kunshan, Suzhou, Shanghai, Shangyu, Haiyan, Jiaxing, and other places. After examination by archaeologists, it is believed that the ancient Wu and Yue cultures were brilliant, and the discovered antiquities are different from those discovered in the north. This proves that ancient Wu and Yue had their own local culture. Last year, archaeologists Wei Juxian, Jin Zutong, Chen Zhiliang, and others visited Jinshan and Yan City to study the antiquities, and the materials obtained were very rich. Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Education Bureau, believes that they are of great value and initiated the Jinshan and Yan City Antiquities Exhibition, which was held at the Municipal People's Education Center the day before yesterday. Over 10,000 people attended the exhibition in two days. Mr. Pan now believes that although antiquities have been discovered in various places, they are scattered and should be part of a comprehensive excavation plan in order to explore the traces of the evolution of ancient Wu and Yue culture. Therefore, he has drafted a plan to send the ancient pottery fragments discovered by Wei to the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The Jiangsu Provincial Government will distribute complete sets of these various pottery fragments, five sets per county, to be displayed in the people's education centers or elementary schools in the five directions of east, south, west, north, and center. If similar antiquities are discovered in various places, excavation can be planned in order to seek comprehensive preservation and organization, so that the antiquities buried underground can be seen by us.

Ministry of Industry Rewards Inventions, Approves Two Patents 99

Ding Ximeng's Ximeng-style Calendar Clock; Shu Zhendong's Chinese Typewriter

The Industrial Technology Examination Committee of the Ministry of Industry has decided that the following inventions will be granted patents for five years: Ding Ximeng's Ximeng-style calendar clock, including the operating month, day, and week mechanism; Shu Zhendong's Zhendong-style Chinese typewriter, including the typing handle, aiming ruler, typing pad, and word spacing grid. In accordance with Article 16 of the Provisional Regulations for Rewarding Industrial Technology, a public announcement will be made. If no interested parties raise objections within six months, the examination will be finalized.

Telegraph Bureau Starts Telephone Telegraph Service Yesterday 100

Satisfactory Results of Three-Month Trial

In order to facilitate users, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications started a trial telephone telegraph service on November 16th last year. The office hours were from 6:00 PM to 7:00 AM the next morning, and after 12:00 noon on Saturdays, telegraphs could be sent. The service was open all day on holidays. Since the start of the trial service, users have found the telephone telegraph service very convenient, and many people have sent telegraphs. The bureau set the trial period to three months. If the results of the trial use were satisfactory, the official telegraph service would be launched. According to the bureau, as of yesterday (the 16th), it has been three months, and the results of the trial telegraph service have been very satisfactory. Therefore, the bureau officially launched the telephone telegraph service yesterday.

French Municipal Council Issues Notice Prohibiting the Sale of Pufferfish 101

The Shanghai French Municipal Council, due to frequent reports of citizens being poisoned by eating pufferfish, has prohibited its sale. The notice states: "Notice: Pufferfish is poisonous and very dangerous to eat. Recently, there have been multiple cases of death due to pufferfish poisoning. Therefore, the sale and cooking of pufferfish must be absolutely prohibited. Residents in all circles must pay attention. This notice."

Married Woman Marries Again After Coming to Shanghai 102

Husband Detects Bigamy and Files Charges

Yin Jinlong married Fan Shuyuan and they have been harmonious for eight years. In April of last year, she came to Shanghai alone to find work. She met a man named Wu Hanzhang and held a marriage ceremony at the Tongshang Hotel on Avenue Edward VII on August 22nd of the same year. They then lived together at 1174 Rue Robert. Yin discovered this and on December 21st of last year, he seized Fan and Wu and took them to the Putuo Road police station. Wu presented a marriage certificate to prove that they were legally married. The police chief ordered Yin to file a lawsuit with the court. Yin then filed a lawsuit with the criminal division of the First Special District Court, accusing Fan Shuyuan and Wu Hanzhang of bigamy, and requested that they be punished in accordance with Article 237 of the law. The court accepted the case, and Judge Liu Yugui opened the eighth criminal court to summon them the other day. Because the defendants had not been summoned, the hearing was adjourned.

Rent Reduction Association Holds Representative Assembly Yesterday 103

Resolution to Request Promulgation of Rent Reduction Measures and Levy Vacant House Tax; Hardoon Tenants to Meet Today to Discuss Measures

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee held a representative assembly yesterday and resolved to request the central government to promulgate rent reduction measures and levy a vacant house tax. Hardoon tenants will hold a meeting today to discuss measures. The detailed report is as follows:

Municipal Rent Reduction Association Representative Assembly

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee convened a representative assembly of various branch associations at 3:00 PM yesterday. Over forty people attended, including Zhang Yichen, Chen Jiufeng, Li Ruzhang, Zhang Xianfang, Ge Futian, and Zheng Shushan. Zhang Yichen, Zhang Xianfang, and Chen Jiufeng were publicly elected as the presidium. The discussion resulted in the following: A letter from the Pudong District Branch, regarding landlords destroying the association's reputation and tearing down slogans, requested assistance. It was resolved to reply to the letter and negotiate with the landlords, and the association will issue a warning. Regarding the Administrative Yuan's joint meeting of various ministries and departments to discuss the Shanghai rent issue and how the association should contribute opinions, it was resolved: (A) To request the Administrative Yuan to promulgate rent reduction measures as soon as possible; (B) Once the rent is legally determined, it should not be increased due to the increase in the value of real estate, which would create double benefits; (C) To suggest that the central government stipulate that the interest on real estate should not exceed 5%; (D) To re-evaluate the land price as soon as possible; (E) To stipulate the rent reduction principle based on the rise and fall of the market; (F) To request the implementation of the vacant house tax. Regarding whether the association should compile the content of its work over the past two years, it was resolved: (A) That various branch associations should separately report the rent reduction situation; (B) To instruct the investigation department to conduct a thorough investigation. Regarding how to stop landlords from forcing tenants to sign new contracts or revise existing contracts when the rental relationship continues to exist, it was resolved: (A) To notify various branch associations to inform members not to be forced to sign contracts, so as not to be bound; (B) To request the court to pay attention and not to judge that there is no rental relationship based on unsigned contracts. Regarding how to make landlords who fail to understand the difficult times aware of the situation, it was resolved: (A) To issue a declaration; (B) To send letters to various radio stations to give speeches on the benefits and harms of the rent reduction movement in Shanghai during broadcasting; (C) To publish a rent reduction special edition, which will be included in the Citizen News supplement every Saturday to save expenses; (D) To notify all members to insist on the spirit of not reducing rent and not paying rent in order to achieve the goal. The Longzhili, Shengpingli, and Daxingfang branch associations requested to negotiate with the landlords. It was resolved to send personnel to negotiate separately. The Deanli Branch reported that the person in charge of the association, He Xitang, was derelict in his duties and missed the deadline for the appeal, and there was suspicion of bribery. It was resolved to send personnel to investigate and organize the matter.

Hardoon Tenants Joint Meeting

The Hardoon Tenants' Joint Rent Reduction Association has scheduled a joint meeting for this afternoon. The notice states: "Greetings, since Shanghai has been affected by the economic downturn, all industries have been declining and life is difficult. Therefore, there has been a vigorous movement to reduce rent. Although the movement has been going on for two years, it has been effective. Most landlords have automatically reduced rent, and there are many cases of rent reduction through mediation. However, the Hardoon Company insists on its views, is rich and unkind, and has failed to make any concessions. Moreover, the rent it sets is expensive, and the conditions are harsh, which is unprecedented for any landlord. Therefore, we have no choice but to invite our fellow tenants who share our suffering to gather together and discuss a comprehensive solution. All Hardoon Company tenants are requested to take time out of their busy schedules to participate in order to achieve the goal of reducing rent. The joint meeting is scheduled for 1:00 PM on the 17th of this month (Monday) at the Citizen's Federation meeting place in the Tianhou Palace Bridge Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The matter concerns your vital interests. Please do not ignore it."

Construction of Public Housing Areas Specifies Construction Principles 104

Different Construction Regulations for Types A and B; License Fees Waived for Self-Built Housing for the Common People

The Shanghai Public Welfare Undertakings Management Committee held its second committee meeting the other day and resolved that the four public housing villages on Zhongshan Road and other places in the city have been completed. Therefore, the construction of two types of public housing areas, A and B, was approved. It is understood that the construction plan is being actively carried out by the executive committee. The regulations on the construction of residential areas have also been stipulated. The regulations include: Type A public housing villages must not build thatched huts or bamboo and wood sheds. Type B public housing villages may build thatched huts and bamboo and wood sheds, but three sides must leave open space of more than three meters wide, and the roofs must be covered with tiles or lead sheets and other non-combustible materials to prevent fires. All houses or sheds must be built three meters away from the road to prepare for future road widening. The construction area must not exceed 50% of the base area, and the height must not exceed one story. If these regulations are exceeded, the municipal government will collect land rent at a higher interest rate. License fees will be waived for common people building single-story houses and sheds themselves, in order to show consideration.

Weather Remains Unstable Until Evening

Since the heavy snow fell on the 5th (Beginning of Spring), the weather has cleared up. Although the climate has been cold and warm, the sky has been clear. However, yesterday morning, a light spring rain fell. By noon, the weather was cloudy and sunny, but the air pressure was still low, the temperature was quite high, the ground was wet, and the weather was still unstable.

Special District Rickshaw Association Holds Meeting of Licensees Yesterday 107

Resolved that Fees Should be Collected According to Regulations and Prices Should Not Be Reduced; Unrentable Vehicles to be Returned to Owners, Effective Yesterday

Due to the departure of most registered rickshaw pullers in the special district, the existing vehicles in each shop could not be fully rented out. The Special District Rickshaw Association has repeatedly negotiated with the Municipal Council to re-register the vehicles to avoid losses, but it has not been approved. Licensees often reduce the rent due to the inability to rent out the vehicles, which has a significant impact on other members. Therefore, the association specially convened a meeting of vehicle owners and licensees yesterday, chaired by Jin Chunlin. As a result of the discussion, it was resolved that the rental of vehicles should be charged in accordance with the regulations of the Municipal Council and that prices should not be reduced. If the vehicles cannot be rented out, they should be returned to the owners. If the owners refuse to accept them, a three-sided notice will be sent to the association for collection. The regulations will be implemented from February 16th. It is also reported that the association plans to request the Municipal Council to re-register rickshaw pullers within a few days.

Zhang Zhijiang Postpones Return to China 108

Still Promoting National Martial Arts in Singapore

Zhang Zhijiang, Director of the Central Martial Arts Academy, went abroad last August to visit Europe and the United States to inspect sports. After completing his work, he went to the Nanyang Islands and telegraphed the students of the physical education program established by the academy to perform national martial arts and basketball to promote and advocate them. At the same time, he raised funds for the school. Pang Yusen led more than a dozen students to the islands. Pang returned to China on the Italian postal ship Conte Verde due to school affairs that needed to be handled, arriving in Shanghai at 7:00 AM on the 16th. Zhang is still in Singapore because he needs to lead the school's students to continue performing. Therefore, he will not return to China for the time being. The rumor that Zhang arrived in Shanghai on the 16th is a misunderstanding of Pang's arrival in Shanghai. It is heard that Zhang is still in Singapore because the school's students' performances have been excellent and warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese. After the performances are completed in Singapore, he will continue to travel to other places. It is expected that he will be able to return to China with the students in two months.

Canton Xiangqin University of Technology Architectural Engineering Study Tour Returns South 109

Thirteen fourth-year students from the Department of Architectural Engineering of Guangdong Provincial Xiangqin University, including Zhu Shaoji, Liang Jingjin, Zhao Xiangqian, Huang Tingzhen, Liang Yaoxiang, Long Bingfen, Zhu Yejin, Chen Jinwen, Guan Weiliang, Wu Gengguang, Zheng Wenji, Yu Shouqi, and Yang Sizhong, organized an architectural engineering study tour led by Professor Hu Deyuan of the university. They arrived in Shanghai on the 28th of last month to study the various architectural contents and structures in the urban and special zones of the city. They also paid attention to urban construction plans and engineering designs related to national defense, such as bridges and roads. Subsequently, on the 6th of this month, they went to Beijing to study the capital's municipal construction and major new buildings. After staying in Beijing for five days, they returned to Shanghai on the 11th and resided at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society on Avenue Albert. In addition to visiting the Guangming Electrical Appliance Thermos Factory on Qingyun Road in Zhabei in recent days, each member of the tour also visited major buildings and residential area architectural designs separately and freely. Having completed their tasks, they took the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiyuan ship at 4 p.m. yesterday, left Shanghai for Hong Kong, and then transferred back to Guangdong. According to Mr. Zhu Shaoji, a member of the tour who spoke to a reporter, the tour's decision to come north for study has provided a wealth of practical knowledge in architectural engineering, and they have benefited greatly. In the future, they will each contribute their knowledge to engage in the architectural engineering business and serve the country and society.

Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Yesterday Sent Letter to Silk Industry to Implement New Dyeing Prices 112

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Trade Association sent a letter to the Silk and Satin Trade Association yesterday regarding the implementation of the metric system and the newly established dyeing prices. The original letter is recorded below: Respectfully, recently, due to the soaring prices of various raw materials such as "pigments" and "coal" needed by our industry, and the high cost, as well as the increasingly excessive and unrestricted lengths of silk cloth, it is a huge loss to calculate by the bolt. Therefore, it was resolved at the general meeting on the 14th of this month that all dyed silk cloth will be priced using the metric system from this year onwards, and a new dyeing price list has been established. The listed prices are all in line with the current economic situation and the policy of unified flat prices, and are based on "monthly settlement" for each industry to facilitate the flow of finance and materials and deeply balance the economic motive of the "silk" and "dyeing" industries. In addition to reporting to the Bureau of Social Affairs for record and sending personnel to obtain approval, we are sending 500 copies of the newly established dyeing price list for your association to check. Please forward them to the members of each group for their information and reply with the processing situation. Respectfully, to the Shanghai Silk and Satin Trade Association.

After the Examination Committee explained, the staff accepted.

Individual interviews will be conducted again by the Supervisory Committee today.

The state-owned China Merchants Bureau, upon the order of the Ministry, is conducting a screening examination for staff. After the Supervisory Committee explained to all staff, it was decided to postpone it to February 23rd and 24th. Individual interviews will be convened again today. The details are as follows:

Supervisory Committee Explains the Significance

Members of the Supervisory Committee Wei Yifu, Ma Xun, Hu Renyuan, Lu Rongguang, Chen Shaoxian, Lu Hanqin, Wu Jizhong, Peng Hu, etc., convened China Merchants Bureau staff Zhu Zengxian, Wu Delin, etc., to explain the significance of the Ministry of Communications' resignation and screening examination. It is reported that all staff have expressed acceptance.

Screening Examination Postponed

The China Merchants Bureau staff screening examination was originally scheduled to be held at 9 a.m. yesterday at Minli Middle School, Dananmen, Zhonghua Road. The reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency went to Minli Middle School yesterday morning and saw ten armed police officers from the Shanghai Public Security Bureau and two police officers from the Wenmiao Road Police Station maintaining order at the entrance. Thieves Wreak Havoc at the Dongxin Bridge Entrance 115

Two thieves squeezed and groped for wallets, and beat the victim after being caught.

Huang Haiping, a native of Hefei who is currently the Director of the Military Law Office of the 39th Army of the stationed Fujian Army and the Supervisory Committee Member of the Special Party Department of the 56th Division, and his adjutant and fellow townsman Wu Xiangli requested leave to return to their hometown. Recently, due to the expiration of their leave, they came to Shanghai from Wuhu by boat and temporarily resided at the residence of a friend named on Beishaxi Road to wait for a ship to return to their posts in Fujian. Huang and Wu took the French-operated Route 5 tram at 5 p.m. on the 14th from the North Railway Station. When they got off at the entrance of Baoyuli, Dongxin Bridge, in the French Concession, thieves Li Youcai (26 years old, native of Funing, residing at No. 9, Deyuli, Beijing Road) and Wu Liansheng (29 years old, residing at No. 7, Xinmin Road, Zhabei) happened to be on the tram and got off at the same time. Li was in front and Wu was behind, squeezing Huang in the middle.

They squeezed desperately, and Wu Liansheng reached into Huang's pocket and stole a wallet containing 15 silver dollars. At that time, Wu Xiangli, Huang's companion, happened to see it from behind. After getting off the tram, he informed Huang that he had been robbed and pointed out the thief. After Huang discovered it, he grabbed the thief Wu Liansheng and demanded the return of the stolen goods. Unexpectedly, the thief not only denied it but also acted aggressively and beat Huang. Wu Xiangli helped to restrain the thief. At this moment, the thief's accomplice Li Youcai came forward and pretended to mediate, insisting that Huang release Wu. Huang refused, and the two sides were arguing, attracting onlookers. Just then, Chinese Constable No. 367 and Russian Constables No. 83 and No. 86 from the French Concession Police Station

arrived on patrol.

After inquiring about the reason, they searched Wu Liansheng's body and found the original stolen wallet. They quickly took him and his accomplice Li Youcai to the police station. It was found that Youcai had committed theft before and had been sentenced to eight months in prison. Wu Liansheng had also been arrested for pickpocketing in the Public Concession and sentenced to three years in prison. He was released on the 17th of last month. Not long after his release, he colluded with accomplices to commit theft again, repeatedly committing crimes without repentance. He was also detained. The day before yesterday, he was escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Special Second District Court. Gu Shouxi, the lawyer of the Police Department, stated the case and requested a postponement to investigate whether other crimes had been committed before requesting an interrogation. It was also reported by Bao Tan Ma Changxin that the defendants were arrested

Investigation Process

and the stolen goods were presented as evidence. Then, the victim Huang Haiping stated that when he got off the tram, two people were squeezing him from the front and back, and he didn't know they were pickpocketing until his companion Wu Xiangli informed him that his wallet had been stolen. He grabbed the second defendant who was stealing. He was very fierce and ordered me to search his body. Finally, he asked me to go to the alley to talk, but I refused. I only wanted him to return my belongings. At that time, the first defendant first persuaded me to let go, then threatened me, and insisted on letting them go. Later, the patrolmen came and

found the stolen goods.

Wu Xiangli also testified that he saw Huang being robbed. When asked, Li Youcai only admitted to mediating and said that he did not know Wu and had no collusion in theft. Wu Liansheng said, "I have already served a three-year sentence, and I am afraid to commit crimes again. It was actually a thief wearing a blue coat and pants and a copper pot hat who committed the theft. The plaintiff insisted that I was stealing." He argued forcefully. The three Chinese and Russian patrolmen who were present were also questioned. Judge Zhang Chaozuo reviewed the testimony and decided to postpone the interrogation to the 19th. The defendants were remanded in custody. The trend of pickpocketing in Shanghai has always been extremely rampant. Since the arrest and imprisonment of the gang leader Xu Datou and others last year, this trend has subsided slightly. Recently, it has revived. It is hoped that the police authorities in the Chinese area will severely crack down on it to ensure the safety of travelers.

Special Commissioner Submits Resignation

Shi Weijun, the Special Commissioner of the China Merchants Bureau, has been in the Bureau for many years and has handled all difficult foreign negotiations with great reputation and is known as a capable person. He has now submitted his resignation. In addition, Zhou Fengtu, the Joint Transportation Commissioner, although reappointed by General Manager Cai as the Deputy Director of the Business Department after resigning to former General Manager Liu, has sent a letter of resignation and has gone north to take up the new position of Deputy Director of the Accounting Department of the Jinpu Railway Bureau.

General Manager Cai Zengji's Written Statement

General Manager Cai Zengji of the China Merchants Bureau issued a written statement saying that the China Merchants Bureau has debts of about 40 million yuan and monthly losses of about 200,000 yuan. The current situation is dangerous, no different from the symptoms of the third stage of lung disease. Therefore, the central government specifically determined thorough rectification measures to treat it. A few months ago, the Executive Yuan handed it over to the Ministry of Railways, Industry, Finance, and Communications to jointly formulate the new regulations of the China Merchants Bureau, which were passed and implemented by the Yuan's decision. These new regulations are no less than the fundamental constitution of the China Merchants Bureau. The original text has been disclosed in the newspapers on the 16th. The regulations stipulate the various organizations and the number of staff of the China Merchants Bureau's head office and branch offices. Therefore, it is necessary to first establish a sound organization based on the new regulations before we can talk about rectification. The Ministry of Communications decided to take the first step in screening the staff of the head office to determine who should stay and who should leave in order to implement the new regulations. In order to avoid solicitation from all parties and strive for fairness, the examination measures were promulgated and scheduled. The examination committee members sent by the Ministry have also arrived in Shanghai ahead of schedule to preside over the matter. However, colleagues in the Bureau, due to the urgent examination time, did not have time to prepare for the examination and sent representatives to request that the examination period be postponed for one week to allow them to prepare calmly, and requested that when those who pass the examination in the future exceed the number of staff required by the Bureau, they should be submitted to the Ministry to determine a placement method. This is reasonable, and I asked Director Lu of the Navigation Administration Department to submit it to the Ministry on my behalf. The Ministry has approved the postponement of the written examination for one week. As for the oral examination, because the examination committee members sent by the Ministry are now in Shanghai, the Ministry advocated holding it first. It is heard that Director Lu decided to explain the first oral examination to colleagues at the Bureau's commemorative week this week. The policy of rectifying the Bureau's affairs and holding screening examinations has been decided by the central government. In this difficult period, under the circumstances of the Bureau, my personal responsibility is only to execute the government's orders. This is not only true for me, but anyone else in my position would do the same. I deeply hope that the Bureau's staff will also understand their own position. They cannot be compared to the staff of ordinary institutions. They are the staff of the government's communications agency. In this extraordinary period, they should have the responsibility to maintain the communications industry as much as possible. It is not permissible for a small number of people to disregard the government's orders for their own selfish interests and use resignation as a threat. If the Bureau's staff or anyone else has good ideas for rectifying the Bureau's affairs and the welfare of all staff, as well as the relief and aftermath of the laid-off staff, and contributes them to the government, I will forward them on their behalf and do my best to ask the government to adopt them, except for those that are unreasonable. If they are confused by the instigation of a small number of unscrupulous elements and attempt to undermine the rectification plan, the government will severely punish them once discovered. If the staff who are law-abiding and conscientious are subject to coercion, they can report the facts, and the government will also protect them. The government's painstaking efforts to rectify the shipping affairs and my responsibility should be understood by the Bureau's staff and the community. Regarding the rectification of the Bureau's affairs, on the passive side, we will first strengthen the organization of the head office and gradually establish credibility before we are qualified to negotiate with creditors and thoroughly rectify the debt repayment methods. The vast majority of the Bureau's assets have been mortgaged to creditors, so we must first have the lowest credibility to make creditors believe in the Bureau's future before we can approach creditors and realize the plans to rectify old debts and raise new capital. I previously decided to go to Beijing to meet with President Jiang of the Executive Yuan and Acting Minister Yu of the Ministry of Communications. They both personally instructed me to break through sentimentality and thoroughly rectify the China Merchants Bureau. The government will be an unlimited backer. All thoughtful and patriotic people should express sympathy for the government authorities' determination. The depth of the Bureau's illness, as mentioned above, has reached its limit. At the beginning of this rectification, without the determination to burn the boats and the spirit of King Yue of Yue in the Spring and Autumn Period to restore the country and the revival of Germany after the European War, we cannot reverse the crisis of the Bureau by striving to implement the central government's policy. But success depends entirely on the Bureau's staff who are well-versed in righteousness, cooperate sincerely, and rely on the community and the government as a strong backing. I am just a public servant of the people, doing my best to carry out their intentions.

Various Chinese and Foreign Circles Mourned Tang Youren Yesterday 116

Funeral today, burial tomorrow

Mr. Tang Youren, former Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Director of the Ministry of Communications, who was shot and killed by thugs on December 25th last year, was encoffined at the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road. Yesterday was the forty-ninth day after his death. The Tang residence specially set up a memorial service at the funeral home to mourn him. No fewer than four hundred people from various Chinese and foreign circles attended the memorial service. President Jiang, Chairman Wang, and others sent elegiac couplets and wreaths. The funeral is scheduled for this morning, and the burial is scheduled for tomorrow afternoon. The details are as follows:

Memorial Service

The hall was set up in the main hall of the funeral home. A portrait of Mr. Tang was placed in front of the coffin, and several dishes of sacrifices were arranged. Cloth curtains were hung outside. The left and right sides of the hall were for guests to rest and were equipped with refreshments. At the entrance of the hall, there was a guest signing area. After signing, guests were led in by reception staff to pay their respects. The inner and outer walls and pillars of the hall were full of elegiac couplets and wreaths sent by various parties. At the entrance of the funeral home, there was a full military band of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The French Concession Police Department sent many detectives to be on alert near the funeral home, as many dignitaries were attending the memorial service. At 6 p.m., the Tang residence held a family memorial service. According to Hunan customs, after the family memorial service, guests present successively held guest memorial services.

Chinese and Foreign Mourners

Those who went to the memorial service yesterday in succession included Wu Tiecheng, Qin Zhen, Zhang Gongquan, Chen Jie, Liu Chengji, a representative of colleagues from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Gao Zongwu, Peng Xuepei, Chuan Rulin, Wang Kemin, Madam Cai Yuanpei, Xu Xiuzhi, Li Zeyi, Yang Hu, Pan Gongzhan, Cai Jinjun, Xu Peihuang, Yang Dezhao, Song Hanzhang, Xu Jiyun, Xu Xinliu, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Guangfu, Bei Songsun, Wang Yansong, Zhou Zuomin, Hu Bijiang, Mei Lanfang, and former Japanese Ambassador to China Arimiyoshi Akira, represented by Ashino, Isogai (Military Attache of the Japanese Embassy), Oki Utsunomiya (Military Assistant Attache), Okino (Naval Assistant Attache), Suma (Japanese Consul General in Beijing), Ishisha (Japanese Consul General in Shanghai), Takasu (Chief of the Third Department of the Naval General Staff of the Japanese Navy), and Kawa (Commander of the Japanese Third Fleet), Kondo (Commander of the Japanese Naval Landing Forces), Kanou (Chairman of the Japanese Residents' Association in Shanghai), as well as relatives and friends of the Tang residence, no fewer than four hundred people.

Mrs. Chen Bijun originally intended to attend Mr. Tang Youren's memorial service at the Shanghai Funeral Home yesterday, but due to a severe cold with a high fever, she entrusted Chu Minyi and Zeng Zhongming to represent Mr. and Mrs. Wang to pay their respects.

Selected Eulogies

Excerpts from the elegiac couplets sent by various parties are as follows: President Jiang: "Inheriting the family's heroic ambition to shine for our party" and "Mourning the loss of a talented person with loyalty and strategy for the country." Chairman of the Central Political Council: "In the midst of a precarious and turbulent situation, he was deeply concerned about the great difficulties that have not yet been resolved. He knew that you would not rest in peace," and "Putting life and death aside, he exhausted his efforts and continued with blood. His sincere connection led to the same return as the martyrs." President Dai Chuanxian: "Waves rise in the seas, using the negotiation table to resolve conflicts in hopes of serving the country," and "Thunder sounds in the clear sky, lamenting the destruction of talents and the elimination of the good." Mayor Wu of this city: "The altar was resounding with fame, but suddenly encountered a tragedy. The seas and the universe are crying together," and "His heroic spirit will last forever, cherishing his former virtue. Yueyun Xiangshui has lingering sorrow." Huang Fu: "Going where others avoid is called isolation. Once the isolation is achieved, the body will inevitably be in danger," and "Acting against the norm reveals a special hardship. Only by suffering can one find peace in death." Xiong Xiling: "In the years of national crisis, I cried for his father in the past, and now I cry for his son. Life is all illusion. Those who congratulate are in the room, and those who mourn are at the door." In addition, military and political figures such as Zhang Xueliang, Yan Xishan, Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, Yu Xuezhong, Yang Yongtai, Chen Guofu, Chen Lifu, Shao Lizi, and Jiang Zuobin, Wang Yongbin, and Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov, Japanese Acting Ambassador Wakasugi, Horiuchi, Arino, Ishisha, and Suma, as well as diplomats from various countries, sent wreaths and couplets, totaling more than six hundred.

Tang's Wife's Memorial Text

Tang's wife, Ouyang Lizheng's memorial text, is full of sorrow and twists and turns, and the words are beautiful and touching. It is worth transcribing the original text as follows: (Omitted above) Alas, the heavens are unkind, destroying my good man. Crying to the heavens and pounding the earth, my head is broken and my heart is shattered. My voice is hoarse and exhausted, and I prostrate myself to offer words. If your spirit is not ignorant, you should be here. Recalling from our marriage to this day, our love has been unwavering, and we have been happy together morning and evening. We have played the plain zither and filled the green liquor. Our lovely daughters and sons have surrounded our knees. We have often said that this happiness is not easy to obtain. We looked forward to growing old together and hiding in the mountains and rivers, hoping to stay away from arrows and avoid nets. How could we have known that from the September 18th Incident to the January 28th Incident, dragons and snakes would run on the land, and the killing intent would be great? You said that in times of national crisis, what could a family do? Every man is responsible, and there is no escape but death. He endured grievances and hardships and did not give in to public opinion. He used the negotiation table to resolve conflicts and had no regrets. Who would defend the country with weapons? He relied on his tongue alone to prevent the passing tide. The responsibility of the whole country was borne by his bare hands, and people still did not understand. Did you die for it? If you die, the country will prosper, and what is there to regret in death? The earth veins are exhausted day by day, and my heart is filled with endless sorrow. Alas, in the afterlife, we can be companions and become ghosts together. The heroic martyrs have a majestic spirit that pierces through the rainbow. As the spirit chariot is about to depart, I grieve for the burial mound. I present the last dried meat and wine and call upon the remaining soul in the emptiness. Soul, return, and partake of the food. Soul, return, and drink. Turning around, I cannot see you, and there is no hope of meeting again. If my body can be redeemed, I would not hesitate to die ten thousand times. Alas, how painful, how painful, we are separated forever. I think of the elderly mother above and pity the young children below. Without this feeling, I would die with you. I look at the southern mountains outside the door and think of the pine trees in the courtyard. My pain is deep and I lack the strength to speak, and my tears are exhausted and there is no blood left to continue. Soul, return, alas, pain, may you enjoy the sacrifice.

Ministry of Transportation Revises the Organizational Charter of the State-Operated China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 118

Full text consists of four chapters, totaling thirty-three articles.

The Ministry of Transportation has revised the organizational charter of the State-Operated China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and promulgated it on the eighth of this month for the bureau to follow. The charter is divided into four chapters, totaling thirty-three articles. The full text is recorded as follows: Revised Organizational Charter of the State-Operated China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Chapter One: General Provisions, Article One: The State-Operated China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is directly under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation and is responsible for domestic and international shipping operations. Article Two: The bureau establishes a head office in the capital or Shanghai, and may establish branch offices or representative offices in various ports as needed, depending on business conditions. Chapter Two: Head Office, Article Three: The bureau has one general manager who oversees all bureau affairs, and two deputy managers who assist the general manager in bureau affairs. All are selected and appointed by the Minister of Transportation. Article Four: The term of office for the general manager and deputy managers is five years and may be renewed upon expiration. The term of office for one of the first deputy managers is three years. Article Five: The general manager may sign the following contracts in the course of daily business, but when entering into contracts for the purchase of materials or construction projects, the regulations of the Ministry of Transportation's affiliated agencies for the purchase of materials or the rules for construction projects shall be applied or followed as appropriate: Contracts for the painting and repair of ships and the purchase of necessary coal and materials. Contracts for the loading and unloading of goods. Contracts for the use of wharves, pontoons, and the storage and delivery of goods. Contracts for the employment of captains, crew members, business managers, and other shipboard service personnel. Contracts for the employment of wharf workers. Contracts for the employment of pilots. Contracts for the leasing of ships, tugboats, and barges. Contracts for commission and advance payment remittance methods for agents selling passenger tickets and soliciting freight on behalf of the bureau. Article Six: The head office establishes three departments: General Affairs, Business Affairs, and Ship Affairs, as well as an Accounting Office and a Treasury. Article Seven: The General Affairs Department is responsible for the following matters: Matters concerning the custody of official seals. Matters concerning the receipt, dispatch, drafting, and archival management of documents. Matters concerning personnel affairs. Matters concerning investigation and statistics. Matters concerning the management of real estate. Matters concerning general affairs. Matters concerning the exploration and storage of ordinary supplies. Other matters not belonging to other departments. Article Eight: The Business Affairs Department is responsible for the following matters: Matters concerning the allocation and dispatch of routes and ships. Matters concerning passenger and freight operations. Matters concerning the operation and management of wharves and warehouses. Matters concerning the business performance evaluation of branch offices. Matters concerning the business performance evaluation of various ships. Other matters concerning business affairs. Article Nine: The Ship Affairs Department is responsible for the following matters: Matters concerning the hiring, firing, and performance evaluation of sailors. Matters concerning the construction and repair of ships. Matters concerning ship equipment. Matters concerning ship inspections. Matters concerning the inspection of various engines and their accessories. Matters concerning the design, inspection, and repair of various electrical and weak electrical equipment. Matters concerning the inspection of fuels and materials. Matters concerning the procurement and storage of fuels and materials. Matters concerning the management of machine factories. Other matters concerning ship affairs. Article Ten: The Treasury is responsible for the following matters: Matters concerning the receipt, disbursement, custody, and registration of funds. Matters concerning the custody of securities, vouchers, contracts, and other documents. Article Eleven: The head office establishes three department heads and one treasury head, who, under the command of the general manager and deputy managers, are responsible for the affairs of their respective departments and treasury. Departments with particularly heavy workloads may establish one deputy head to assist the department head in their duties. Article Twelve: The head office employs 60 to 70 clerks and assistants, and 12 to 14 accountants. Article Thirteen: Each department of the head office may divide tasks into sections for handling. Article Fourteen: The head office employs two secretaries to handle confidential matters. Article Fifteen: The head office employs two to four engineers to handle technical matters. Article Sixteen: The department heads, deputy heads, and engineers of the bureau are appointed by the Ministry of Transportation. The secretaries are appointed by the general manager after submitting a request to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article Seventeen: The clerks and assistants of the head office are all assigned by the general manager and reported to the Ministry of Transportation for record. Article Eighteen: Personnel responsible for technical matters in each department should be filled by technical personnel. Article Nineteen: The accounting affairs of the head office are managed by the Accounting Office, the organization of which will be determined separately. Article Twenty: The head office may hire consultants under the command of the Ministry of Transportation. Chapter Three: Branch Offices and Representative Offices, Article Twenty-One: Branch offices and representative offices are established by the general manager after submitting a request to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article Twenty-Two: Branch offices and representative offices are divided into the following grades according to the complexity of their business and the amount of their income, and are approved by the Ministry of Transportation upon request by the general manager: Branch offices: First-class branch offices, Second-class branch offices, Third-class branch offices; Representative offices: First-class representative offices, Second-class representative offices, Third-class representative offices. Article Twenty-Three: Branch offices are subordinate to the head office, and representative offices are subordinate to branch offices or directly to the head office. The business jurisdiction of each branch office is approved by the Ministry of Transportation upon request by the general manager. Article Twenty-Four: Each branch office has one manager appointed by the Ministry of Transportation, and each representative office has one section chief appointed by the general manager after submitting a request to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article Twenty-Five: Branch offices may establish the following sections and offices: General Affairs Section, Business Affairs Section, Accounting Office. Article Twenty-Six: Branch offices and representative offices employ clerks and assistants, the number of which is based on the following standards: Branch offices: First-class branch offices: 10 to 15 people, Second-class branch offices: 8 to 12 people, Third-class branch offices: 6 to 9 people; Representative offices: First-class representative offices: 4 to 6 people, Second-class representative offices: 3 to 5 people, Third-class representative offices: 2 to 4 people. The personnel mentioned above are all assigned by the general manager and reported to the Ministry of Transportation for record. Article Twenty-Seven: The business operations of branch offices and representative offices must not adopt a contract-based system. However, in commercial ports where bureaus and offices have not been established, the general manager may request the Ministry of Transportation for approval to entrust agents to act on their behalf and give them appropriate commissions. Chapter Four: Supplementary Provisions, Article Twenty-Eight: The business progress of the bureau shall be compiled into reports on a regular basis and submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for review. Article Twenty-Nine: The salary grades of the head office, branch office, and representative office staff shall be approved by the Ministry of Transportation. Article Thirty: The entire budget of the bureau shall be submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article Thirty-One: The distribution of the bureau's year-end surplus shall be submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. Article Thirty-Two: The bureau may formulate other detailed rules and regulations and submit them to the Ministry of Transportation for approval and implementation. Article Thirty-Three: This charter shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.
